=== Example 0 ===
Prompt:
The following is a first-order logic (FOL) problem.
The problem is to determine whether the conclusion follows from the premises.
The premises are given in the form of a set of first-order logic sentences.
The conclusion is given in the form of a single first-order logic sentence.
The task is to translate each of the premises and conclusions into FOL expressions.and then to evaluate the conclusion as ANSWER: True, ANSWER: False, or ANSWER: Uncertain given the premises. The output should follow format TEXT: 
FOL: 
TEXT: 
FOL:... ANSWER: 


<PREMISES>
All biodegradable things are environment-friendly.
All woodware is biodegradable.
All paper is woodware.
Nothing is a good thing and also a bad thing.
All environment-friendly things are good.
A worksheet is either paper or environment-friendly.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
A worksheet is not biodegradable.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>
TEXT: All biodegradable things are environment-friendly.
FOL: all x. (Biodegradable(x) -> EnvironmentFriendly(x))
TEXT: All woodware is biodegradable.
FOL: all x. (Woodware(x) -> Biodegradable(x))
TEXT: All paper is woodware.
FOL: all x. (Paper(x) -> Woodware(x))
TEXT: Nothing is a good thing and also a bad thing.
FOL: -(exists x. (Good(x) & Bad(x)))
TEXT: All environment-friendly things are good.
FOL: all x. (EnvironmentFriendly(x) -> Good(x))
TEXT: A worksheet is either paper or environment-friendly.
FOL: ((Paper(Worksheet) & -EnvironmentFriendly(Worksheet)) | (-Paper(Worksheet) & EnvironmentFriendly(Worksheet)))
TEXT: A worksheet is not biodegradable.
FOL: -Dispensable(Worksheet)

ANSWER: Uncertain
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
A La Liga soccer team ranks higher than another La Liga soccer team if it receives more points.
If there are two La Liga soccer teams and neither has more points than the other, then the team which receives more points from the games between the two teams ranks higher.
Real Madrid and Barcelona are both La Liga soccer teams.
Real Madrid received more points than Barcelona.
Neither Real Madrid nor Barcelona received more points from the games between them.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
Real Madrid ranks higher than Barcelona.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>
TEXT: A La Liga soccer team ranks higher than another La Liga soccer team if it receives more points.
FOL: all x. all y. (LaLigaSoccerTeam(x) & LaLigaSoccerTeam(y) & MorePoints(x, y) -> RankHigherThan(x, y))
TEXT: If there are two La Liga soccer teams and neither has more points than the other, then the team which receives more points from the games between the two teams ranks higher.
FOL: all x. all y. (LaLigaSoccerTeam(x) & LaLigaSoccerTeam(y) & -MorePoints(x, y) & -MorePoints(y, x) & MorePointsInGameBetween(x, y) ->  RankHigherThan(x, y))
TEXT: Real Madrid and Barcelona are both La Liga soccer teams.
FOL: LaLigaSoccerTeam(RealMadrid) & LaLigaSoccerTeam(Barcelona)
TEXT: Real Madrid received more points than Barcelona.
FOL: MorePoints(RealMadrid, Barcelona)
TEXT: Neither Real Madrid nor Barcelona received more points from the games between them.
FOL: -MorePointsInGameBetween(RealMadrid, Barcelona) & -MorePointsInGameBetween(Barcelona, RealMadrid)
TEXT: Real Madrid ranks higher than Barcelona.
FOL: HigherRank(RealMadrid, Barcelona)

ANSWER: True
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
All professional athletes spend most of their time on sports.
All Olympic gold medal winners are professional athletes.
No full-time scientists spend the majority of their time on sports.
All Nobel physics laureates are full-time scientists.
Amy spends the most time on sports, or Amy is an Olympic gold medal winner.
If Amy is not a Nobel physics laureate, then Amy is not an Olympic gold medal winner.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
If Amy is not an Olympic gold medal winner, then Amy is a Nobel physics laureate.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>
TEXT: All professional athletes spend most of their time on sports.
FOL: all x. (ProfessionalAthlete(x) -> SpendOn(x, MostOfTheirTime, Sports))
TEXT: All Olympic gold medal winners are professional athletes.
FOL: all x. (OlympicGoldMedalWinner(x) -> ProfessionalAthlete(x))
TEXT: No full-time scientists spend the majority of their time on sports.
FOL: all x. (FullTimeScientist(x) -> -SpendOn(x, MostOfTheirTime, Sports))
TEXT: All Nobel physics laureates are full-time scientists.
FOL: all x. (NobelPhysicsLaureate(x) -> FullTimeScientist(x))
TEXT: Amy spends the most time on sports, or Amy is an Olympic gold medal winner.
FOL: SpendOn(Amy, MostOfTheirTime, Sports) | OlympicGoldMedalWinner(Amy)
TEXT: If Amy is not a Nobel physics laureate, then Amy is not an Olympic gold medal winner.
FOL: -NobelPhysicsLaureate(Amy) -> -OlympicGoldMedalWinner(Amy)
TEXT: If Amy is not an Olympic gold medal winner, then Amy is a Nobel physics laureate.
FOL: -OlympicGoldMedalWinner(Amy) -> NobelLaureate(Amy)

ANSWER: False
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
Miroslav Venhoda was a Czech choral conductor who specialized in the performance of Renaissance and Baroque music.
Any choral conductor is a musician.
Some musicians love music.
Miroslav Venhoda published a book in 1946 called Method of Studying Gregorian Chant.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
No choral conductor specialized in the performance of Renaissance.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>

Generation 1:
TEXT: Miroslav Venhoda was a Czech choral conductor who specialized in the performance of Renaissance and Baroque music.
FOL: ChoralConductor(Venhoda) & SpecializesIn(Venhoda, PerformanceOfRenaissanceMusic) & SpecializesIn(Venhoda, PerformanceOfBaroqueMusic)
TEXT: Any choral conductor is a musician.
FOL: all x. (ChoralConductor(x) -> Musician(x))
TEXT: Some musicians love music.
FOL: exists x. (Musician(x) & Loves(x, Music))
TEXT: Miroslav Venhoda published a book in 1946 called "Method of Studying Gregorian Chant."
FOL: Published(Venhoda, Book, "Method of Studying Gregorian Chant", 1946)
TEXT: No choral conductor specialized in the performance of Renaissance.
FOL: -exists x. (ChoralConductor(x) & SpecializesIn(x, PerformanceOfRenaissanceMusic))

ANSWER: False

Explanation:
The premise explicitly states that Miroslav Venhoda, a choral conductor, specializes in the performance of Renaissance music. Therefore, the conclusion that no choral conductor specialized in the performance of Renaissance music directly contradicts this premise. Hence, the answer is False.
Processed: False

Generation 2:
TEXT: Miroslav Venhoda was a Czech choral conductor who specialized in the performance of Renaissance and Baroque music.
FOL: ChoralConductor(Venhoda) & SpecializesIn(Venhoda, Performance(Renaissance)) & SpecializesIn(Venhoda, Performance(Baroque))
TEXT: Any choral conductor is a musician.
FOL: all x. (ChoralConductor(x) -> Musician(x))
TEXT: Some musicians love music.
FOL: exists x. (Musician(x) & Love(x, Music))
TEXT: Miroslav Venhoda published a book in 1946 called Method of Studying Gregorian Chant.
FOL: PublishedBook(Venhoda, "Method of Studying Gregorian Chant", 1946)
TEXT: No choral conductor specialized in the performance of Renaissance.
FOL: -exists x. (ChoralConductor(x) & SpecializesIn(x, Performance(Renaissance)))

ANSWER: False

Explanation:
The conclusion is directly contradicted by the first premise which states that Miroslav Venhoda was a choral conductor who specialized in the performance of Renaissance music. Thus, the conclusion is false given the provided premises.
Processed: False

Generation 3:
TEXT: Miroslav Venhoda was a Czech choral conductor who specialized in the performance of Renaissance and Baroque music.
FOL: ChoralConductor(MiroslavVenhoda) & SpecializedIn(MiroslavVenhoda, Performance, Renaissance) & SpecializedIn(MiroslavVenhoda, Performance, Baroque)
TEXT: Any choral conductor is a musician.
FOL: all x. (ChoralConductor(x) -> Musician(x))
TEXT: Some musicians love music.
FOL: exists x. (Musician(x) & Love(x, Music))
TEXT: Miroslav Venhoda published a book in 1946 called Method of Studying Gregorian Chant.
FOL: PublishedBook(MiroslavVenhoda, "Method of Studying Gregorian Chant", 1946)

TEXT: No choral conductor specialized in the performance of Renaissance.
FOL: -(exists x. (ChoralConductor(x) & SpecializedIn(x, Performance, Renaissance)))

ANSWER: False

Explanation: From the first premise, we know that Miroslav Venhoda is a choral conductor who specialized in the performance of Renaissance music. Therefore, the statement "No choral conductor specialized in the performance of Renaissance" is directly contradicted by this information, making the conclusion false.
Processed: False

Generation 4:
TEXT: Miroslav Venhoda was a Czech choral conductor who specialized in the performance of Renaissance and Baroque music.
FOL: ChoralConductor(MiroslavVenhoda) & SpecializesIn(MiroslavVenhoda, RenaissanceMusic) & SpecializesIn(MiroslavVenhoda, BaroqueMusic)
TEXT: Any choral conductor is a musician.
FOL: all x. (ChoralConductor(x) -> Musician(x))
TEXT: Some musicians love music.
FOL: exists x. (Musician(x) & Loves(x, Music))
TEXT: Miroslav Venhoda published a book in 1946 called Method of Studying Gregorian Chant.
FOL: PublishedBook(MiroslavVenhoda, "Method of Studying Gregorian Chant", 1946)

TEXT: No choral conductor specialized in the performance of Renaissance.
FOL: -(exists x. (ChoralConductor(x) & SpecializesIn(x, RenaissanceMusic)))

ANSWER: False

Explanation:
Given that Miroslav Venhoda, who is identified as a choral conductor, specializes in Renaissance music, the conclusion that no choral conductor specializes in Renaissance music contradicts this information directly. Therefore, the conclusion does not logically follow from the premises, making it false.
Processed: False

Generation 5:
TEXT: Miroslav Venhoda was a Czech choral conductor who specialized in the performance of Renaissance and Baroque music.
FOL: ChoralConductor(Venhoda) & SpecializesIn(Venhoda, Renaissance) & SpecializesIn(Venhoda, Baroque)
TEXT: Any choral conductor is a musician.
FOL: all x. (ChoralConductor(x) -> Musician(x))
TEXT: Some musicians love music.
FOL: exists x. (Musician(x) & Loves(x, Music))
TEXT: Miroslav Venhoda published a book in 1946 called Method of Studying Gregorian Chant.
FOL: PublishedBook(Venhoda, "Method of Studying Gregorian Chant", 1946)
TEXT: No choral conductor specialized in the performance of Renaissance.
FOL: -exists x. (ChoralConductor(x) & SpecializesIn(x, Renaissance))

ANSWER: False

Explanation:
The conclusion contradicts one of the premises. According to the premises, Miroslav Venhoda, who is a choral conductor, specialized in the performance of Renaissance music. Therefore, the statement that no choral conductor specialized in the performance of Renaissance is false based on the information provided.
Processed: False

Reference: False

=== Example 1 ===
Prompt:
The following is a first-order logic (FOL) problem.
The problem is to determine whether the conclusion follows from the premises.
The premises are given in the form of a set of first-order logic sentences.
The conclusion is given in the form of a single first-order logic sentence.
The task is to translate each of the premises and conclusions into FOL expressions.and then to evaluate the conclusion as ANSWER: True, ANSWER: False, or ANSWER: Uncertain given the premises. The output should follow format TEXT: 
FOL: 
TEXT: 
FOL:... ANSWER: 


<PREMISES>
All biodegradable things are environment-friendly.
All woodware is biodegradable.
All paper is woodware.
Nothing is a good thing and also a bad thing.
All environment-friendly things are good.
A worksheet is either paper or environment-friendly.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
A worksheet is not biodegradable.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>
TEXT: All biodegradable things are environment-friendly.
FOL: all x. (Biodegradable(x) -> EnvironmentFriendly(x))
TEXT: All woodware is biodegradable.
FOL: all x. (Woodware(x) -> Biodegradable(x))
TEXT: All paper is woodware.
FOL: all x. (Paper(x) -> Woodware(x))
TEXT: Nothing is a good thing and also a bad thing.
FOL: -(exists x. (Good(x) & Bad(x)))
TEXT: All environment-friendly things are good.
FOL: all x. (EnvironmentFriendly(x) -> Good(x))
TEXT: A worksheet is either paper or environment-friendly.
FOL: ((Paper(Worksheet) & -EnvironmentFriendly(Worksheet)) | (-Paper(Worksheet) & EnvironmentFriendly(Worksheet)))
TEXT: A worksheet is not biodegradable.
FOL: -Dispensable(Worksheet)

ANSWER: Uncertain
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
A La Liga soccer team ranks higher than another La Liga soccer team if it receives more points.
If there are two La Liga soccer teams and neither has more points than the other, then the team which receives more points from the games between the two teams ranks higher.
Real Madrid and Barcelona are both La Liga soccer teams.
Real Madrid received more points than Barcelona.
Neither Real Madrid nor Barcelona received more points from the games between them.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
Real Madrid ranks higher than Barcelona.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>
TEXT: A La Liga soccer team ranks higher than another La Liga soccer team if it receives more points.
FOL: all x. all y. (LaLigaSoccerTeam(x) & LaLigaSoccerTeam(y) & MorePoints(x, y) -> RankHigherThan(x, y))
TEXT: If there are two La Liga soccer teams and neither has more points than the other, then the team which receives more points from the games between the two teams ranks higher.
FOL: all x. all y. (LaLigaSoccerTeam(x) & LaLigaSoccerTeam(y) & -MorePoints(x, y) & -MorePoints(y, x) & MorePointsInGameBetween(x, y) ->  RankHigherThan(x, y))
TEXT: Real Madrid and Barcelona are both La Liga soccer teams.
FOL: LaLigaSoccerTeam(RealMadrid) & LaLigaSoccerTeam(Barcelona)
TEXT: Real Madrid received more points than Barcelona.
FOL: MorePoints(RealMadrid, Barcelona)
TEXT: Neither Real Madrid nor Barcelona received more points from the games between them.
FOL: -MorePointsInGameBetween(RealMadrid, Barcelona) & -MorePointsInGameBetween(Barcelona, RealMadrid)
TEXT: Real Madrid ranks higher than Barcelona.
FOL: HigherRank(RealMadrid, Barcelona)

ANSWER: True
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
All professional athletes spend most of their time on sports.
All Olympic gold medal winners are professional athletes.
No full-time scientists spend the majority of their time on sports.
All Nobel physics laureates are full-time scientists.
Amy spends the most time on sports, or Amy is an Olympic gold medal winner.
If Amy is not a Nobel physics laureate, then Amy is not an Olympic gold medal winner.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
If Amy is not an Olympic gold medal winner, then Amy is a Nobel physics laureate.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>
TEXT: All professional athletes spend most of their time on sports.
FOL: all x. (ProfessionalAthlete(x) -> SpendOn(x, MostOfTheirTime, Sports))
TEXT: All Olympic gold medal winners are professional athletes.
FOL: all x. (OlympicGoldMedalWinner(x) -> ProfessionalAthlete(x))
TEXT: No full-time scientists spend the majority of their time on sports.
FOL: all x. (FullTimeScientist(x) -> -SpendOn(x, MostOfTheirTime, Sports))
TEXT: All Nobel physics laureates are full-time scientists.
FOL: all x. (NobelPhysicsLaureate(x) -> FullTimeScientist(x))
TEXT: Amy spends the most time on sports, or Amy is an Olympic gold medal winner.
FOL: SpendOn(Amy, MostOfTheirTime, Sports) | OlympicGoldMedalWinner(Amy)
TEXT: If Amy is not a Nobel physics laureate, then Amy is not an Olympic gold medal winner.
FOL: -NobelPhysicsLaureate(Amy) -> -OlympicGoldMedalWinner(Amy)
TEXT: If Amy is not an Olympic gold medal winner, then Amy is a Nobel physics laureate.
FOL: -OlympicGoldMedalWinner(Amy) -> NobelLaureate(Amy)

ANSWER: False
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
Some fish stings people.
Stonefish is a fish.
Stonefish stings when stepped on.
If a stonefish stings someone and they are not treated, it can cause death to them.
To treat stonefish stings, apply heat to the affected area or use an antivenom.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
Stings of some fish can cause death if not treated.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>

Generation 1:
TEXT: Some fish stings people.
FOL: exists x. (Fish(x) & Stings(x, somePerson))
TEXT: Stonefish is a fish.
FOL: Fish(Stonefish)
TEXT: Stonefish stings when stepped on.
FOL: SteppedOn(somePerson, Stonefish) -> Stings(Stonefish, somePerson)
TEXT: If a stonefish stings someone and they are not treated, it can cause death to them.
FOL: Stings(Stonefish, somePerson) & -Treated(somePerson) -> Death(somePerson)
TEXT: To treat stonefish stings, apply heat to the affected area or use an antivenom.
FOL: Treated(somePerson) <- (ApplyHeat(somePerson) | UseAntivenom(somePerson))
TEXT: Stings of some fish can cause death if not treated.
FOL: exists x. (Fish(x) & Stings(x, somePerson) & -Treated(somePerson) -> Death(somePerson))

ANSWER: True

Explanation: From the premises, we know that "some fish stings people" and that the specific example of a stonefish can cause death if its sting is untreated. Since the conclusion is about "some fish" and we have an example that satisfies this condition (stonefish), the conclusion logically follows from the premises. Therefore, the answer is True.
Processed: True

Generation 2:
TEXT: Some fish stings people.
FOL: exists x. (Fish(x) & Stings(x, person))
TEXT: Stonefish is a fish.
FOL: Fish(Stonefish)
TEXT: Stonefish stings when stepped on.
FOL: SteppedOn(person, Stonefish) -> Stings(Stonefish, person)
TEXT: If a stonefish stings someone and they are not treated, it can cause death to them.
FOL: Stings(Stonefish, person) & -Treated(person) -> Death(person)
TEXT: To treat stonefish stings, apply heat to the affected area or use an antivenom.
FOL: Treated(person) <-> (ApplyHeat(person) | UseAntivenom(person))
TEXT: Stings of some fish can cause death if not treated.
FOL: exists x. (Fish(x) & Stings(x, person) & -Treated(person) -> Death(person))

ANSWER: True

Explanation: From the premises, we know that Stonefish, which is a fish, can sting a person and potentially cause death if not treated. Since Stonefish is an example of a fish whose sting can be fatal if untreated, the conclusion that "stings of some fish can cause death if not treated" logically follows from the premises. Therefore, the answer is True.
Processed: True

Generation 3:
TEXT: Some fish stings people.
FOL: exists x. (Fish(x) & Stings(x, People))
TEXT: Stonefish is a fish.
FOL: Fish(Stonefish)
TEXT: Stonefish stings when stepped on.
FOL: StingsWhenSteppedOn(Stonefish)
TEXT: If a stonefish stings someone and they are not treated, it can cause death to them.
FOL: all x. (Person(x) & Stings(Stonefish, x) & NotTreated(x) -> Death(x))
TEXT: To treat stonefish stings, apply heat to the affected area or use an antivenom.
FOL: TreatmentForStonefishSting(x) -> ApplyHeat(x) | UseAntivenom(x)
TEXT: Stings of some fish can cause death if not treated.
FOL: exists x. (Fish(x) & Stings(x, People) & NotTreated(People) -> Death(People))

ANSWER: True

Explanation:
Given that Stonefish is a fish and its sting can cause death if not treated, this directly implies that the stings of at least one type of fish (the Stonefish) can cause death if left untreated. Therefore, the conclusion logically follows from the premises provided.
Processed: True

Generation 4:
TEXT: Some fish stings people.
FOL: exists x. (Fish(x) & Stings(x, somePerson))

TEXT: Stonefish is a fish.
FOL: Fish(Stonefish)

TEXT: Stonefish stings when stepped on.
FOL: SteppedOn(Stonefish) -> Stings(Stonefish, someone)

TEXT: If a stonefish stings someone and they are not treated, it can cause death to them.
FOL: Stings(Stonefish, someone) & NotTreated(someone) -> CanCauseDeath(someone)

TEXT: To treat stonefish stings, apply heat to the affected area or use an antivenom.
FOL: TreatsStonefishSting(ApplyHeat, someone) | TreatsStonefishSting(UseAntivenom, someone)

TEXT: Stings of some fish can cause death if not treated.
FOL: exists x. (Fish(x) & Stings(x, someone) & NotTreated(someone) -> CanCauseDeath(someone))

ANSWER: True

Explanation:
Given the premises, we know that a Stonefish is a type of fish and its sting, if untreated, can cause death. This directly satisfies the conclusion's statement that "stings of some fish can cause death if not treated," where "some fish" can be satisfied by the specific example of Stonefish. Therefore, the conclusion logically follows from the premises provided.
Processed: True

Generation 5:
TEXT: Some fish stings people.
FOL: exists x. (Fish(x) & Stings(x, someone))

TEXT: Stonefish is a fish.
FOL: Fish(Stonefish)

TEXT: If a stonefish stings someone and they are not treated, it can cause death to them.
FOL: Stings(Stonefish, someone) & NotTreated(someone) -> CanCauseDeath(someone)

FOL: TreatmentMethod(stonefish_sting, apply_heat) | TreatmentMethod(stonefish_sting, use_antivenom)

TEXT: Stings of some fish can cause death if not treated.
FOL: exists x. (Fish(x) & Stings(x, someone) & NotTreated(someone) -> CanCauseDeath(someone))

ANSWER: True

Explanation: The conclusion follows from the premises because one of the premises specifically states that if a stonefish stings someone and they are not treated, it can cause death. Since stonefish is a fish, we have an instance of a fish (stonefish) whose sting can cause death if untreated, which supports the conclusion.
Processed: True

Reference: True

=== Example 2 ===
Prompt:
The following is a first-order logic (FOL) problem.

The conclusion is given in the form of a single first-order logic sentence.

<PREMISES>

TEXT: All paper is woodware.
FOL: all x. (Paper(x) -> Woodware(x))

FOL: -(exists x. (Good(x) & Bad(x)))

FOL: ((Paper(Worksheet) & -EnvironmentFriendly(Worksheet)) | (-Paper(Worksheet) & EnvironmentFriendly(Worksheet)))

<PREMISES>

FOL: -MorePointsInGameBetween(RealMadrid, Barcelona) & -MorePointsInGameBetween(Barcelona, RealMadrid)
TEXT: Real Madrid ranks higher than Barcelona.
FOL: HigherRank(RealMadrid, Barcelona)

ANSWER: True
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
All professional athletes spend most of their time on sports.
All Olympic gold medal winners are professional athletes.
No full-time scientists spend the majority of their time on sports.
All Nobel physics laureates are full-time scientists.
Amy spends the most time on sports, or Amy is an Olympic gold medal winner.
If Amy is not a Nobel physics laureate, then Amy is not an Olympic gold medal winner.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
If Amy is not an Olympic gold medal winner, then Amy is a Nobel physics laureate.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>

FOL: all x. (ProfessionalAthlete(x) -> SpendOn(x, MostOfTheirTime, Sports))
TEXT: All Olympic gold medal winners are professional athletes.
FOL: all x. (OlympicGoldMedalWinner(x) -> ProfessionalAthlete(x))
TEXT: No full-time scientists spend the majority of their time on sports.
FOL: all x. (FullTimeScientist(x) -> -SpendOn(x, MostOfTheirTime, Sports))
TEXT: All Nobel physics laureates are full-time scientists.
FOL: all x. (NobelPhysicsLaureate(x) -> FullTimeScientist(x))

FOL: SpendOn(Amy, MostOfTheirTime, Sports) | OlympicGoldMedalWinner(Amy)
TEXT: If Amy is not a Nobel physics laureate, then Amy is not an Olympic gold medal winner.
FOL: -NobelPhysicsLaureate(Amy) -> -OlympicGoldMedalWinner(Amy)
TEXT: If Amy is not an Olympic gold medal winner, then Amy is a Nobel physics laureate.
FOL: -OlympicGoldMedalWinner(Amy) -> NobelLaureate(Amy)

ANSWER: False
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
All bears in zoos are not wild.
Some bears are in zoos.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
Not all bears are wild.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>

Generation 1:
TEXT: All bears in zoos are not wild.
FOL: all x. (BearInZoo(x) -> -Wild(x))
TEXT: Some bears are in zoos.
FOL: exists x. (Bear(x) & BearInZoo(x))
TEXT: Not all bears are wild.
FOL: -(all x. (Bear(x) -> Wild(x)))

ANSWER: True

This means the conclusion "Not all bears are wild" logically follows from the premises.

=== Example 3 ===
Prompt:
The following is a first-order logic (FOL) problem.
The problem is to determine whether the conclusion follows from the premises.
The premises are given in the form of a set of first-order logic sentences.
The conclusion is given in the form of a single first-order logic sentence.
The task is to translate each of the premises and conclusions into FOL expressions.and then to evaluate the conclusion as ANSWER: True, ANSWER: False, or ANSWER: Uncertain given the premises. The output should follow format TEXT: 
FOL: 
TEXT: 
FOL:... ANSWER: 


<PREMISES>
All biodegradable things are environment-friendly.
All woodware is biodegradable.
All paper is woodware.
Nothing is a good thing and also a bad thing.
All environment-friendly things are good.
A worksheet is either paper or environment-friendly.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
A worksheet is not biodegradable.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>
TEXT: All biodegradable things are environment-friendly.
FOL: all x. (Biodegradable(x) -> EnvironmentFriendly(x))
TEXT: All woodware is biodegradable.
FOL: all x. (Woodware(x) -> Biodegradable(x))
TEXT: All paper is woodware.
FOL: all x. (Paper(x) -> Woodware(x))
TEXT: Nothing is a good thing and also a bad thing.
FOL: -(exists x. (Good(x) & Bad(x)))
TEXT: All environment-friendly things are good.
FOL: all x. (EnvironmentFriendly(x) -> Good(x))
TEXT: A worksheet is either paper or environment-friendly.
FOL: ((Paper(Worksheet) & -EnvironmentFriendly(Worksheet)) | (-Paper(Worksheet) & EnvironmentFriendly(Worksheet)))
TEXT: A worksheet is not biodegradable.
FOL: -Dispensable(Worksheet)

ANSWER: Uncertain
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
A La Liga soccer team ranks higher than another La Liga soccer team if it receives more points.
If there are two La Liga soccer teams and neither has more points than the other, then the team which receives more points from the games between the two teams ranks higher.
Real Madrid and Barcelona are both La Liga soccer teams.
Real Madrid received more points than Barcelona.
Neither Real Madrid nor Barcelona received more points from the games between them.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
Real Madrid ranks higher than Barcelona.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>
TEXT: A La Liga soccer team ranks higher than another La Liga soccer team if it receives more points.
FOL: all x. all y. (LaLigaSoccerTeam(x) & LaLigaSoccerTeam(y) & MorePoints(x, y) -> RankHigherThan(x, y))
TEXT: If there are two La Liga soccer teams and neither has more points than the other, then the team which receives more points from the games between the two teams ranks higher.
FOL: all x. all y. (LaLigaSoccerTeam(x) & LaLigaSoccerTeam(y) & -MorePoints(x, y) & -MorePoints(y, x) & MorePointsInGameBetween(x, y) ->  RankHigherThan(x, y))
TEXT: Real Madrid and Barcelona are both La Liga soccer teams.
FOL: LaLigaSoccerTeam(RealMadrid) & LaLigaSoccerTeam(Barcelona)
TEXT: Real Madrid received more points than Barcelona.
FOL: MorePoints(RealMadrid, Barcelona)
TEXT: Neither Real Madrid nor Barcelona received more points from the games between them.
FOL: -MorePointsInGameBetween(RealMadrid, Barcelona) & -MorePointsInGameBetween(Barcelona, RealMadrid)
TEXT: Real Madrid ranks higher than Barcelona.
FOL: HigherRank(RealMadrid, Barcelona)

ANSWER: True
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
All professional athletes spend most of their time on sports.
All Olympic gold medal winners are professional athletes.
No full-time scientists spend the majority of their time on sports.
All Nobel physics laureates are full-time scientists.
Amy spends the most time on sports, or Amy is an Olympic gold medal winner.
If Amy is not a Nobel physics laureate, then Amy is not an Olympic gold medal winner.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
If Amy is not an Olympic gold medal winner, then Amy is a Nobel physics laureate.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>
TEXT: All professional athletes spend most of their time on sports.
FOL: all x. (ProfessionalAthlete(x) -> SpendOn(x, MostOfTheirTime, Sports))
TEXT: All Olympic gold medal winners are professional athletes.
FOL: all x. (OlympicGoldMedalWinner(x) -> ProfessionalAthlete(x))
TEXT: No full-time scientists spend the majority of their time on sports.
FOL: all x. (FullTimeScientist(x) -> -SpendOn(x, MostOfTheirTime, Sports))
TEXT: All Nobel physics laureates are full-time scientists.
FOL: all x. (NobelPhysicsLaureate(x) -> FullTimeScientist(x))
TEXT: Amy spends the most time on sports, or Amy is an Olympic gold medal winner.
FOL: SpendOn(Amy, MostOfTheirTime, Sports) | OlympicGoldMedalWinner(Amy)
TEXT: If Amy is not a Nobel physics laureate, then Amy is not an Olympic gold medal winner.
FOL: -NobelPhysicsLaureate(Amy) -> -OlympicGoldMedalWinner(Amy)
TEXT: If Amy is not an Olympic gold medal winner, then Amy is a Nobel physics laureate.
FOL: -OlympicGoldMedalWinner(Amy) -> NobelLaureate(Amy)

ANSWER: False
</EVALUATE>

=== Example 6 ===
Prompt:
The following is a first-order logic (FOL) problem.
The problem is to determine whether the conclusion follows from the premises.
The premises are given in the form of a set of first-order logic sentences.
The conclusion is given in the form of a single first-order logic sentence.
The task is to translate each of the premises and conclusions into FOL expressions.and then to evaluate the conclusion as ANSWER: True, ANSWER: False, or ANSWER: Uncertain given the premises. The output should follow format TEXT: 
FOL: 
TEXT: 
FOL:... ANSWER: 


<PREMISES>
All biodegradable things are environment-friendly.
All woodware is biodegradable.
All paper is woodware.
Nothing is a good thing and also a bad thing.
All environment-friendly things are good.
A worksheet is either paper or environment-friendly.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
A worksheet is not biodegradable.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>
TEXT: All biodegradable things are environment-friendly.
FOL: all x. (Biodegradable(x) -> EnvironmentFriendly(x))
TEXT: All woodware is biodegradable.
FOL: all x. (Woodware(x) -> Biodegradable(x))
TEXT: All paper is woodware.
FOL: all x. (Paper(x) -> Woodware(x))
TEXT: Nothing is a good thing and also a bad thing.
FOL: -(exists x. (Good(x) & Bad(x)))
TEXT: All environment-friendly things are good.
FOL: all x. (EnvironmentFriendly(x) -> Good(x))
TEXT: A worksheet is either paper or environment-friendly.
FOL: ((Paper(Worksheet) & -EnvironmentFriendly(Worksheet)) | (-Paper(Worksheet) & EnvironmentFriendly(Worksheet)))
TEXT: A worksheet is not biodegradable.
FOL: -Dispensable(Worksheet)

ANSWER: Uncertain
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
A La Liga soccer team ranks higher than another La Liga soccer team if it receives more points.
If there are two La Liga soccer teams and neither has more points than the other, then the team which receives more points from the games between the two teams ranks higher.
Real Madrid and Barcelona are both La Liga soccer teams.
Real Madrid received more points than Barcelona.
Neither Real Madrid nor Barcelona received more points from the games between them.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
Real Madrid ranks higher than Barcelona.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>
TEXT: A La Liga soccer team ranks higher than another La Liga soccer team if it receives more points.
FOL: all x. all y. (LaLigaSoccerTeam(x) & LaLigaSoccerTeam(y) & MorePoints(x, y) -> RankHigherThan(x, y))
TEXT: If there are two La Liga soccer teams and neither has more points than the other, then the team which receives more points from the games between the two teams ranks higher.
FOL: all x. all y. (LaLigaSoccerTeam(x) & LaLigaSoccerTeam(y) & -MorePoints(x, y) & -MorePoints(y, x) & MorePointsInGameBetween(x, y) ->  RankHigherThan(x, y))
TEXT: Real Madrid and Barcelona are both La Liga soccer teams.
FOL: LaLigaSoccerTeam(RealMadrid) & LaLigaSoccerTeam(Barcelona)
TEXT: Real Madrid received more points than Barcelona.
FOL: MorePoints(RealMadrid, Barcelona)
TEXT: Neither Real Madrid nor Barcelona received more points from the games between them.
FOL: -MorePointsInGameBetween(RealMadrid, Barcelona) & -MorePointsInGameBetween(Barcelona, RealMadrid)
TEXT: Real Madrid ranks higher than Barcelona.
FOL: HigherRank(RealMadrid, Barcelona)

ANSWER: True
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
All professional athletes spend most of their time on sports.
All Olympic gold medal winners are professional athletes.
No full-time scientists spend the majority of their time on sports.
All Nobel physics laureates are full-time scientists.
Amy spends the most time on sports, or Amy is an Olympic gold medal winner.
If Amy is not a Nobel physics laureate, then Amy is not an Olympic gold medal winner.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
If Amy is not an Olympic gold medal winner, then Amy is a Nobel physics laureate.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>

FOL: all x. (ProfessionalAthlete(x) -> SpendOn(x, MostOfTheirTime, Sports))

TEXT: If Amy is not a Nobel physics laureate, then Amy is not an Olympic gold medal winner.
FOL: -NobelPhysicsLaureate(Amy) -> -OlympicGoldMedalWinner(Amy)
TEXT: If Amy is not an Olympic gold medal winner, then Amy is a Nobel physics laureate.
FOL: -OlympicGoldMedalWinner(Amy) -> NobelLaureate(Amy)

ANSWER: False
</EVALUATE>

The following is a first-order logic (FOL) problem.
The problem is to determine whether the conclusion follows from the premises.
The premises are given in the form of a set of first-order logic sentences.
The conclusion is given in the form of a single first-order logic sentence.
The task is to translate each of the premises and conclusions into FOL expressions.and then to evaluate the conclusion as ANSWER: True, ANSWER: False, or ANSWER: Uncertain given the premises. The output should follow format TEXT: 
FOL: 
TEXT: 
FOL:... ANSWER: 


<PREMISES>
All biodegradable things are environment-friendly.
All woodware is biodegradable.
All paper is woodware.
Nothing is a good thing and also a bad thing.
All environment-friendly things are good.
A worksheet is either paper or environment-friendly.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
A worksheet is not biodegradable.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>
TEXT: All biodegradable things are environment-friendly.
FOL: all x. (Biodegradable(x) -> EnvironmentFriendly(x))
TEXT: All woodware is biodegradable.
FOL: all x. (Woodware(x) -> Biodegradable(x))
TEXT: All paper is woodware.
FOL: all x. (Paper(x) -> Woodware(x))
TEXT: Nothing is a good thing and also a bad thing.
FOL: -(exists x. (Good(x) & Bad(x)))

TEXT: A worksheet is either paper or environment-friendly.
FOL: ((Paper(Worksheet) & -EnvironmentFriendly(Worksheet)) | (-Paper(Worksheet) & EnvironmentFriendly(Worksheet)))
TEXT: A worksheet is not biodegradable.
FOL: -Dispensable(Worksheet)

ANSWER: Uncertain
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
A La Liga soccer team ranks higher than another La Liga soccer team if it receives more points.
If there are two La Liga soccer teams and neither has more points than the other, then the team which receives more points from the games between the two teams ranks higher.
Real Madrid and Barcelona are both La Liga soccer teams.
Real Madrid received more points than Barcelona.
Neither Real Madrid nor Barcelona received more points from the games between them.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
Real Madrid ranks higher than Barcelona.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>
TEXT: A La Liga soccer team ranks higher than another La Liga soccer team if it receives more points.
FOL: all x. all y. (LaLigaSoccerTeam(x) & LaLigaSoccerTeam(y) & MorePoints(x, y) -> RankHigherThan(x, y))
TEXT: If there are two La Liga soccer teams and neither has more points than the other, then the team which receives more points from the games between the two teams ranks higher.
FOL: all x. all y. (LaLigaSoccerTeam(x) & LaLigaSoccerTeam(y) & -MorePoints(x, y) & -MorePoints(y, x) & MorePointsInGameBetween(x, y) ->  RankHigherThan(x, y))
TEXT: Real Madrid and Barcelona are both La Liga soccer teams.
FOL: LaLigaSoccerTeam(RealMadrid) & LaLigaSoccerTeam(Barcelona)
TEXT: Real Madrid received more points than Barcelona.
FOL: MorePoints(RealMadrid, Barcelona)
TEXT: Neither Real Madrid nor Barcelona received more points from the games between them.
FOL: -MorePointsInGameBetween(RealMadrid, Barcelona) & -MorePointsInGameBetween(Barcelona, RealMadrid)
TEXT: Real Madrid ranks higher than Barcelona.
FOL: HigherRank(RealMadrid, Barcelona)

ANSWER: True
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>

All Olympic gold medal winners are professional athletes.
No full-time scientists spend the majority of their time on sports.
All Nobel physics laureates are full-time scientists.

</PREMISES>

ANSWER: False
</EVALUATE>

=== Example 11 ===
Prompt:
The following is a first-order logic (FOL) problem.
The problem is to determine whether the conclusion follows from the premises.
The premises are given in the form of a set of first-order logic sentences.
The conclusion is given in the form of a single first-order logic sentence.
The task is to translate each of the premises and conclusions into FOL expressions.and then to evaluate the conclusion as ANSWER: True, ANSWER: False, or ANSWER: Uncertain given the premises. The output should follow format TEXT: 
FOL: 
TEXT: 
FOL:... ANSWER: 


<PREMISES>
All biodegradable things are environment-friendly.
All woodware is biodegradable.
All paper is woodware.
Nothing is a good thing and also a bad thing.
All environment-friendly things are good.
A worksheet is either paper or environment-friendly.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
A worksheet is not biodegradable.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>
TEXT: All biodegradable things are environment-friendly.
FOL: all x. (Biodegradable(x) -> EnvironmentFriendly(x))
TEXT: All woodware is biodegradable.
FOL: all x. (Woodware(x) -> Biodegradable(x))
TEXT: All paper is woodware.
FOL: all x. (Paper(x) -> Woodware(x))
TEXT: Nothing is a good thing and also a bad thing.
FOL: -(exists x. (Good(x) & Bad(x)))
TEXT: All environment-friendly things are good.
FOL: all x. (EnvironmentFriendly(x) -> Good(x))
TEXT: A worksheet is either paper or environment-friendly.
FOL: ((Paper(Worksheet) & -EnvironmentFriendly(Worksheet)) | (-Paper(Worksheet) & EnvironmentFriendly(Worksheet)))
TEXT: A worksheet is not biodegradable.
FOL: -Dispensable(Worksheet)

ANSWER: Uncertain
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
A La Liga soccer team ranks higher than another La Liga soccer team if it receives more points.
If there are two La Liga soccer teams and neither has more points than the other, then the team which receives more points from the games between the two teams ranks higher.
Real Madrid and Barcelona are both La Liga soccer teams.
Real Madrid received more points than Barcelona.
Neither Real Madrid nor Barcelona received more points from the games between them.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
Real Madrid ranks higher than Barcelona.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>
TEXT: A La Liga soccer team ranks higher than another La Liga soccer team if it receives more points.
FOL: all x. all y. (LaLigaSoccerTeam(x) & LaLigaSoccerTeam(y) & MorePoints(x, y) -> RankHigherThan(x, y))
TEXT: If there are two La Liga soccer teams and neither has more points than the other, then the team which receives more points from the games between the two teams ranks higher.
FOL: all x. all y. (LaLigaSoccerTeam(x) & LaLigaSoccerTeam(y) & -MorePoints(x, y) & -MorePoints(y, x) & MorePointsInGameBetween(x, y) ->  RankHigherThan(x, y))
TEXT: Real Madrid and Barcelona are both La Liga soccer teams.
FOL: LaLigaSoccerTeam(RealMadrid) & LaLigaSoccerTeam(Barcelona)
TEXT: Real Madrid received more points than Barcelona.
FOL: MorePoints(RealMadrid, Barcelona)
TEXT: Neither Real Madrid nor Barcelona received more points from the games between them.
FOL: -MorePointsInGameBetween(RealMadrid, Barcelona) & -MorePointsInGameBetween(Barcelona, RealMadrid)
TEXT: Real Madrid ranks higher than Barcelona.
FOL: HigherRank(RealMadrid, Barcelona)

ANSWER: True
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
All professional athletes spend most of their time on sports.
All Olympic gold medal winners are professional athletes.
No full-time scientists spend the majority of their time on sports.
All Nobel physics laureates are full-time scientists.
Amy spends the most time on sports, or Amy is an Olympic gold medal winner.
If Amy is not a Nobel physics laureate, then Amy is not an Olympic gold medal winner.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
If Amy is not an Olympic gold medal winner, then Amy is a Nobel physics laureate.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>
TEXT: All professional athletes spend most of their time on sports.
FOL: all x. (ProfessionalAthlete(x) -> SpendOn(x, MostOfTheirTime, Sports))
TEXT: All Olympic gold medal winners are professional athletes.
FOL: all x. (OlympicGoldMedalWinner(x) -> ProfessionalAthlete(x))
TEXT: No full-time scientists spend the majority of their time on sports.
FOL: all x. (FullTimeScientist(x) -> -SpendOn(x, MostOfTheirTime, Sports))
TEXT: All Nobel physics laureates are full-time scientists.
FOL: all x. (NobelPhysicsLaureate(x) -> FullTimeScientist(x))
TEXT: Amy spends the most time on sports, or Amy is an Olympic gold medal winner.
FOL: SpendOn(Amy, MostOfTheirTime, Sports) | OlympicGoldMedalWinner(Amy)
TEXT: If Amy is not a Nobel physics laureate, then Amy is not an Olympic gold medal winner.
FOL: -NobelPhysicsLaureate(Amy) -> -OlympicGoldMedalWinner(Amy)
TEXT: If Amy is not an Olympic gold medal winner, then Amy is a Nobel physics laureate.
FOL: -OlympicGoldMedalWinner(Amy) -> NobelLaureate(Amy)

ANSWER: False
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>

</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
No phones are electronic.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>

FOL: all x. (Phone(x) -> -Electronic(x))

ANSWER: False

Explanation:
Given the premises, we know that all iPhones are electronic and some phones are indeed iPhones. Thus, it must be true that some phones are electronic. Therefore, the conclusion stating that no phones are electronic contradicts the given premises and is thus false.

=== Example 14 ===
Prompt:
The following is a first-order logic (FOL) problem.
The problem is to determine whether the conclusion follows from the premises.
The premises are given in the form of a set of first-order logic sentences.
The conclusion is given in the form of a single first-order logic sentence.
The task is to translate each of the premises and conclusions into FOL expressions.and then to evaluate the conclusion as ANSWER: True, ANSWER: False, or ANSWER: Uncertain given the premises. The output should follow format TEXT: 
FOL: 
TEXT: 
FOL:... ANSWER: 


<PREMISES>
All biodegradable things are environment-friendly.
All woodware is biodegradable.
All paper is woodware.
Nothing is a good thing and also a bad thing.
All environment-friendly things are good.
A worksheet is either paper or environment-friendly.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
A worksheet is not biodegradable.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>
TEXT: All biodegradable things are environment-friendly.
FOL: all x. (Biodegradable(x) -> EnvironmentFriendly(x))
TEXT: All woodware is biodegradable.
FOL: all x. (Woodware(x) -> Biodegradable(x))
TEXT: All paper is woodware.
FOL: all x. (Paper(x) -> Woodware(x))
TEXT: Nothing is a good thing and also a bad thing.
FOL: -(exists x. (Good(x) & Bad(x)))
TEXT: All environment-friendly things are good.
FOL: all x. (EnvironmentFriendly(x) -> Good(x))
TEXT: A worksheet is either paper or environment-friendly.
FOL: ((Paper(Worksheet) & -EnvironmentFriendly(Worksheet)) | (-Paper(Worksheet) & EnvironmentFriendly(Worksheet)))
TEXT: A worksheet is not biodegradable.
FOL: -Dispensable(Worksheet)

ANSWER: Uncertain
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
A La Liga soccer team ranks higher than another La Liga soccer team if it receives more points.
If there are two La Liga soccer teams and neither has more points than the other, then the team which receives more points from the games between the two teams ranks higher.
Real Madrid and Barcelona are both La Liga soccer teams.
Real Madrid received more points than Barcelona.
Neither Real Madrid nor Barcelona received more points from the games between them.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
Real Madrid ranks higher than Barcelona.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>
TEXT: A La Liga soccer team ranks higher than another La Liga soccer team if it receives more points.
FOL: all x. all y. (LaLigaSoccerTeam(x) & LaLigaSoccerTeam(y) & MorePoints(x, y) -> RankHigherThan(x, y))
TEXT: If there are two La Liga soccer teams and neither has more points than the other, then the team which receives more points from the games between the two teams ranks higher.
FOL: all x. all y. (LaLigaSoccerTeam(x) & LaLigaSoccerTeam(y) & -MorePoints(x, y) & -MorePoints(y, x) & MorePointsInGameBetween(x, y) ->  RankHigherThan(x, y))
TEXT: Real Madrid and Barcelona are both La Liga soccer teams.
FOL: LaLigaSoccerTeam(RealMadrid) & LaLigaSoccerTeam(Barcelona)
TEXT: Real Madrid received more points than Barcelona.
FOL: MorePoints(RealMadrid, Barcelona)
TEXT: Neither Real Madrid nor Barcelona received more points from the games between them.
FOL: -MorePointsInGameBetween(RealMadrid, Barcelona) & -MorePointsInGameBetween(Barcelona, RealMadrid)
TEXT: Real Madrid ranks higher than Barcelona.
FOL: HigherRank(RealMadrid, Barcelona)

ANSWER: True
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>

All Olympic gold medal winners are professional athletes.

If Amy is not a Nobel physics laureate, then Amy is not an Olympic gold medal winner.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
If Amy is not an Olympic gold medal winner, then Amy is a Nobel physics laureate.
</CONCLUSION>

TEXT: If Amy is not a Nobel physics laureate, then Amy is not an Olympic gold medal winner.
FOL: -NobelPhysicsLaureate(Amy) -> -OlympicGoldMedalWinner(Amy)
TEXT: If Amy is not an Olympic gold medal winner, then Amy is a Nobel physics laureate.

ANSWER: False
</EVALUATE>

=== Example 16 ===
Prompt:
The following is a first-order logic (FOL) problem.
The problem is to determine whether the conclusion follows from the premises.
The premises are given in the form of a set of first-order logic sentences.
The conclusion is given in the form of a single first-order logic sentence.

FOL: 
TEXT: 
FOL:... ANSWER:

All woodware is biodegradable.
All paper is woodware.
Nothing is a good thing and also a bad thing.
All environment-friendly things are good.

</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
A worksheet is not biodegradable.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>

FOL: all x. (Biodegradable(x) -> EnvironmentFriendly(x))
TEXT: All woodware is biodegradable.

TEXT: All paper is woodware.

TEXT: A worksheet is either paper or environment-friendly.
FOL: ((Paper(Worksheet) & -EnvironmentFriendly(Worksheet)) | (-Paper(Worksheet) & EnvironmentFriendly(Worksheet)))
TEXT: A worksheet is not biodegradable.
FOL: -Dispensable(Worksheet)

ANSWER: Uncertain
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
A La Liga soccer team ranks higher than another La Liga soccer team if it receives more points.
If there are two La Liga soccer teams and neither has more points than the other, then the team which receives more points from the games between the two teams ranks higher.
Real Madrid and Barcelona are both La Liga soccer teams.
Real Madrid received more points than Barcelona.
Neither Real Madrid nor Barcelona received more points from the games between them.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
Real Madrid ranks higher than Barcelona.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>
TEXT: A La Liga soccer team ranks higher than another La Liga soccer team if it receives more points.

TEXT: Neither Real Madrid nor Barcelona received more points from the games between them.
FOL: -MorePointsInGameBetween(RealMadrid, Barcelona) & -MorePointsInGameBetween(Barcelona, RealMadrid)
TEXT: Real Madrid ranks higher than Barcelona.
FOL: HigherRank(RealMadrid, Barcelona)

ANSWER: True
</EVALUATE>

The problem is to determine whether the conclusion follows from the premises.
The premises are given in the form of a set of first-order logic sentences.
The conclusion is given in the form of a single first-order logic sentence.
The task is to translate each of the premises and conclusions into FOL expressions.and then to evaluate the conclusion as ANSWER: True, ANSWER: False, or ANSWER: Uncertain given the premises. The output should follow format TEXT: 
FOL: 
TEXT: 
FOL:... ANSWER: 


<PREMISES>
All biodegradable things are environment-friendly.
All woodware is biodegradable.
All paper is woodware.
Nothing is a good thing and also a bad thing.
All environment-friendly things are good.
A worksheet is either paper or environment-friendly.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
A worksheet is not biodegradable.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>
TEXT: All biodegradable things are environment-friendly.
FOL: all x. (Biodegradable(x) -> EnvironmentFriendly(x))
TEXT: All woodware is biodegradable.
FOL: all x. (Woodware(x) -> Biodegradable(x))
TEXT: All paper is woodware.
FOL: all x. (Paper(x) -> Woodware(x))
TEXT: Nothing is a good thing and also a bad thing.
FOL: -(exists x. (Good(x) & Bad(x)))
TEXT: All environment-friendly things are good.
FOL: all x. (EnvironmentFriendly(x) -> Good(x))
TEXT: A worksheet is either paper or environment-friendly.
FOL: ((Paper(Worksheet) & -EnvironmentFriendly(Worksheet)) | (-Paper(Worksheet) & EnvironmentFriendly(Worksheet)))
TEXT: A worksheet is not biodegradable.
FOL: -Dispensable(Worksheet)

ANSWER: Uncertain
</EVALUATE>

=== Example 21 ===
Prompt:
The following is a first-order logic (FOL) problem.
The problem is to determine whether the conclusion follows from the premises.
The premises are given in the form of a set of first-order logic sentences.
The conclusion is given in the form of a single first-order logic sentence.
The task is to translate each of the premises and conclusions into FOL expressions.and then to evaluate the conclusion as ANSWER: True, ANSWER: False, or ANSWER: Uncertain given the premises. The output should follow format TEXT: 
FOL: 
TEXT: 
FOL:... ANSWER: 


<PREMISES>
All biodegradable things are environment-friendly.
All woodware is biodegradable.
All paper is woodware.
Nothing is a good thing and also a bad thing.
All environment-friendly things are good.
A worksheet is either paper or environment-friendly.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
A worksheet is not biodegradable.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>
TEXT: All biodegradable things are environment-friendly.
FOL: all x. (Biodegradable(x) -> EnvironmentFriendly(x))
TEXT: All woodware is biodegradable.
FOL: all x. (Woodware(x) -> Biodegradable(x))
TEXT: All paper is woodware.
FOL: all x. (Paper(x) -> Woodware(x))
TEXT: Nothing is a good thing and also a bad thing.
FOL: -(exists x. (Good(x) & Bad(x)))
TEXT: All environment-friendly things are good.
FOL: all x. (EnvironmentFriendly(x) -> Good(x))
TEXT: A worksheet is either paper or environment-friendly.
FOL: ((Paper(Worksheet) & -EnvironmentFriendly(Worksheet)) | (-Paper(Worksheet) & EnvironmentFriendly(Worksheet)))
TEXT: A worksheet is not biodegradable.
FOL: -Dispensable(Worksheet)

ANSWER: Uncertain
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
A La Liga soccer team ranks higher than another La Liga soccer team if it receives more points.
If there are two La Liga soccer teams and neither has more points than the other, then the team which receives more points from the games between the two teams ranks higher.
Real Madrid and Barcelona are both La Liga soccer teams.
Real Madrid received more points than Barcelona.
Neither Real Madrid nor Barcelona received more points from the games between them.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
Real Madrid ranks higher than Barcelona.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>
TEXT: A La Liga soccer team ranks higher than another La Liga soccer team if it receives more points.
FOL: all x. all y. (LaLigaSoccerTeam(x) & LaLigaSoccerTeam(y) & MorePoints(x, y) -> RankHigherThan(x, y))
TEXT: If there are two La Liga soccer teams and neither has more points than the other, then the team which receives more points from the games between the two teams ranks higher.
FOL: all x. all y. (LaLigaSoccerTeam(x) & LaLigaSoccerTeam(y) & -MorePoints(x, y) & -MorePoints(y, x) & MorePointsInGameBetween(x, y) ->  RankHigherThan(x, y))
TEXT: Real Madrid and Barcelona are both La Liga soccer teams.
FOL: LaLigaSoccerTeam(RealMadrid) & LaLigaSoccerTeam(Barcelona)
TEXT: Real Madrid received more points than Barcelona.
FOL: MorePoints(RealMadrid, Barcelona)
TEXT: Neither Real Madrid nor Barcelona received more points from the games between them.
FOL: -MorePointsInGameBetween(RealMadrid, Barcelona) & -MorePointsInGameBetween(Barcelona, RealMadrid)
TEXT: Real Madrid ranks higher than Barcelona.
FOL: HigherRank(RealMadrid, Barcelona)

ANSWER: True
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
All professional athletes spend most of their time on sports.
All Olympic gold medal winners are professional athletes.
No full-time scientists spend the majority of their time on sports.
All Nobel physics laureates are full-time scientists.
Amy spends the most time on sports, or Amy is an Olympic gold medal winner.
If Amy is not a Nobel physics laureate, then Amy is not an Olympic gold medal winner.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
If Amy is not an Olympic gold medal winner, then Amy is a Nobel physics laureate.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>
TEXT: All professional athletes spend most of their time on sports.
FOL: all x. (ProfessionalAthlete(x) -> SpendOn(x, MostOfTheirTime, Sports))
TEXT: All Olympic gold medal winners are professional athletes.
FOL: all x. (OlympicGoldMedalWinner(x) -> ProfessionalAthlete(x))
TEXT: No full-time scientists spend the majority of their time on sports.
FOL: all x. (FullTimeScientist(x) -> -SpendOn(x, MostOfTheirTime, Sports))
TEXT: All Nobel physics laureates are full-time scientists.
FOL: all x. (NobelPhysicsLaureate(x) -> FullTimeScientist(x))

FOL: SpendOn(Amy, MostOfTheirTime, Sports) | OlympicGoldMedalWinner(Amy)
TEXT: If Amy is not a Nobel physics laureate, then Amy is not an Olympic gold medal winner.
FOL: -NobelPhysicsLaureate(Amy) -> -OlympicGoldMedalWinner(Amy)
TEXT: If Amy is not an Olympic gold medal winner, then Amy is a Nobel physics laureate.
FOL: -OlympicGoldMedalWinner(Amy) -> NobelLaureate(Amy)

ANSWER: False
</EVALUATE>

TEXT: Eight is the double of four.
FOL: Equals(Eight, Double(Four))

TEXT: Four is the double of two.
FOL: Equals(Four, Double(Two))

TEXT: Six is larger than seven.
FOL: Larger(Six, Seven)

ANSWER: False

Explanation:
- From "Seven equals six plus one", we have that `Equals(Seven, Plus(Six, One))`. According to the premise "If a real number equals another real number added by one, the first number is larger", this implies that `Larger(Seven, Six)`.
- Therefore, the statement "Six is larger than seven" (`Larger(Six, Seven)`) contradicts with `Larger(Seven, Six)`, making it false.

The conclusion is given in the form of a single first-order logic sentence.

FOL: 
TEXT: 
FOL:... ANSWER:

All biodegradable things are environment-friendly.

All paper is woodware.
Nothing is a good thing and also a bad thing.

</PREMISES>

A worksheet is not biodegradable.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>

FOL: all x. (Biodegradable(x) -> EnvironmentFriendly(x))

TEXT: All paper is woodware.

FOL: ((Paper(Worksheet) & -EnvironmentFriendly(Worksheet)) | (-Paper(Worksheet) & EnvironmentFriendly(Worksheet)))
TEXT: A worksheet is not biodegradable.
FOL: -Dispensable(Worksheet)

ANSWER: Uncertain
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
A La Liga soccer team ranks higher than another La Liga soccer team if it receives more points.
If there are two La Liga soccer teams and neither has more points than the other, then the team which receives more points from the games between the two teams ranks higher.
Real Madrid and Barcelona are both La Liga soccer teams.
Real Madrid received more points than Barcelona.
Neither Real Madrid nor Barcelona received more points from the games between them.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
Real Madrid ranks higher than Barcelona.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>

FOL: all x. all y. (LaLigaSoccerTeam(x) & LaLigaSoccerTeam(y) & MorePoints(x, y) -> RankHigherThan(x, y))
TEXT: If there are two La Liga soccer teams and neither has more points than the other, then the team which receives more points from the games between the two teams ranks higher.

FOL: LaLigaSoccerTeam(RealMadrid) & LaLigaSoccerTeam(Barcelona)

FOL: MorePoints(RealMadrid, Barcelona)
TEXT: Neither Real Madrid nor Barcelona received more points from the games between them.
FOL: -MorePointsInGameBetween(RealMadrid, Barcelona) & -MorePointsInGameBetween(Barcelona, RealMadrid)
TEXT: Real Madrid ranks higher than Barcelona.
FOL: HigherRank(RealMadrid, Barcelona)

ANSWER: True
</EVALUATE>

FOL: VolunteerDisasterResponse(x) -> ReceiveIntangibleBenefits(x)

ANSWER: True

(Volunteer(x) -> ReceiveIntangibleBenefits(x))). TEXT:

<PREMISES>

All woodware is biodegradable.

Nothing is a good thing and also a bad thing.

<EVALUATE>

FOL: all x. (Woodware(x) -> Biodegradable(x))
TEXT: All paper is woodware.

TEXT: Nothing is a good thing and also a bad thing.
FOL: -(exists x. (Good(x) & Bad(x)))

FOL: all x. (EnvironmentFriendly(x) -> Good(x))
TEXT: A worksheet is either paper or environment-friendly.
FOL: ((Paper(Worksheet) & -EnvironmentFriendly(Worksheet)) | (-Paper(Worksheet) & EnvironmentFriendly(Worksheet)))
TEXT: A worksheet is not biodegradable.
FOL: -Dispensable(Worksheet)

ANSWER: Uncertain
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
A La Liga soccer team ranks higher than another La Liga soccer team if it receives more points.
If there are two La Liga soccer teams and neither has more points than the other, then the team which receives more points from the games between the two teams ranks higher.
Real Madrid and Barcelona are both La Liga soccer teams.
Real Madrid received more points than Barcelona.
Neither Real Madrid nor Barcelona received more points from the games between them.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
Real Madrid ranks higher than Barcelona.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>
TEXT: A La Liga soccer team ranks higher than another La Liga soccer team if it receives more points.
FOL: all x. all y. (LaLigaSoccerTeam(x) & LaLigaSoccerTeam(y) & MorePoints(x, y) -> RankHigherThan(x, y))
TEXT: If there are two La Liga soccer teams and neither has more points than the other, then the team which receives more points from the games between the two teams ranks higher.
FOL: all x. all y. (LaLigaSoccerTeam(x) & LaLigaSoccerTeam(y) & -MorePoints(x, y) & -MorePoints(y, x) & MorePointsInGameBetween(x, y) ->  RankHigherThan(x, y))
TEXT: Real Madrid and Barcelona are both La Liga soccer teams.

TEXT: Real Madrid received more points than Barcelona.
FOL: MorePoints(RealMadrid, Barcelona)
TEXT: Neither Real Madrid nor Barcelona received more points from the games between them.
FOL: -MorePointsInGameBetween(RealMadrid, Barcelona) & -MorePointsInGameBetween(Barcelona, RealMadrid)
TEXT: Real Madrid ranks higher than Barcelona.
FOL: HigherRank(RealMadrid, Barcelona)

ANSWER: True
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
All professional athletes spend most of their time on sports.
All Olympic gold medal winners are professional athletes.
No full-time scientists spend the majority of their time on sports.
All Nobel physics laureates are full-time scientists.

=== Example 28 ===
Prompt:
The following is a first-order logic (FOL) problem.
The problem is to determine whether the conclusion follows from the premises.
The premises are given in the form of a set of first-order logic sentences.
The conclusion is given in the form of a single first-order logic sentence.
The task is to translate each of the premises and conclusions into FOL expressions.and then to evaluate the conclusion as ANSWER: True, ANSWER: False, or ANSWER: Uncertain given the premises. The output should follow format TEXT: 
FOL: 
TEXT: 
FOL:... ANSWER: 


<PREMISES>
All biodegradable things are environment-friendly.
All woodware is biodegradable.
All paper is woodware.
Nothing is a good thing and also a bad thing.
All environment-friendly things are good.
A worksheet is either paper or environment-friendly.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
A worksheet is not biodegradable.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>
TEXT: All biodegradable things are environment-friendly.
FOL: all x. (Biodegradable(x) -> EnvironmentFriendly(x))
TEXT: All woodware is biodegradable.
FOL: all x. (Woodware(x) -> Biodegradable(x))
TEXT: All paper is woodware.
FOL: all x. (Paper(x) -> Woodware(x))
TEXT: Nothing is a good thing and also a bad thing.
FOL: -(exists x. (Good(x) & Bad(x)))
TEXT: All environment-friendly things are good.
FOL: all x. (EnvironmentFriendly(x) -> Good(x))
TEXT: A worksheet is either paper or environment-friendly.
FOL: ((Paper(Worksheet) & -EnvironmentFriendly(Worksheet)) | (-Paper(Worksheet) & EnvironmentFriendly(Worksheet)))
TEXT: A worksheet is not biodegradable.
FOL: -Dispensable(Worksheet)

ANSWER: Uncertain
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
A La Liga soccer team ranks higher than another La Liga soccer team if it receives more points.
If there are two La Liga soccer teams and neither has more points than the other, then the team which receives more points from the games between the two teams ranks higher.
Real Madrid and Barcelona are both La Liga soccer teams.
Real Madrid received more points than Barcelona.
Neither Real Madrid nor Barcelona received more points from the games between them.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
Real Madrid ranks higher than Barcelona.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>
TEXT: A La Liga soccer team ranks higher than another La Liga soccer team if it receives more points.
FOL: all x. all y. (LaLigaSoccerTeam(x) & LaLigaSoccerTeam(y) & MorePoints(x, y) -> RankHigherThan(x, y))
TEXT: If there are two La Liga soccer teams and neither has more points than the other, then the team which receives more points from the games between the two teams ranks higher.
FOL: all x. all y. (LaLigaSoccerTeam(x) & LaLigaSoccerTeam(y) & -MorePoints(x, y) & -MorePoints(y, x) & MorePointsInGameBetween(x, y) ->  RankHigherThan(x, y))
TEXT: Real Madrid and Barcelona are both La Liga soccer teams.
FOL: LaLigaSoccerTeam(RealMadrid) & LaLigaSoccerTeam(Barcelona)
TEXT: Real Madrid received more points than Barcelona.
FOL: MorePoints(RealMadrid, Barcelona)
TEXT: Neither Real Madrid nor Barcelona received more points from the games between them.
FOL: -MorePointsInGameBetween(RealMadrid, Barcelona) & -MorePointsInGameBetween(Barcelona, RealMadrid)
TEXT: Real Madrid ranks higher than Barcelona.
FOL: HigherRank(RealMadrid, Barcelona)

ANSWER: True
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
All professional athletes spend most of their time on sports.
All Olympic gold medal winners are professional athletes.
No full-time scientists spend the majority of their time on sports.
All Nobel physics laureates are full-time scientists.
Amy spends the most time on sports, or Amy is an Olympic gold medal winner.
If Amy is not a Nobel physics laureate, then Amy is not an Olympic gold medal winner.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
If Amy is not an Olympic gold medal winner, then Amy is a Nobel physics laureate.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>
TEXT: All professional athletes spend most of their time on sports.
FOL: all x. (ProfessionalAthlete(x) -> SpendOn(x, MostOfTheirTime, Sports))
TEXT: All Olympic gold medal winners are professional athletes.
FOL: all x. (OlympicGoldMedalWinner(x) -> ProfessionalAthlete(x))
TEXT: No full-time scientists spend the majority of their time on sports.
FOL: all x. (FullTimeScientist(x) -> -SpendOn(x, MostOfTheirTime, Sports))
TEXT: All Nobel physics laureates are full-time scientists.
FOL: all x. (NobelPhysicsLaureate(x) -> FullTimeScientist(x))
TEXT: Amy spends the most time on sports, or Amy is an Olympic gold medal winner.
FOL: SpendOn(Amy, MostOfTheirTime, Sports) | OlympicGoldMedalWinner(Amy)
TEXT: If Amy is not a Nobel physics laureate, then Amy is not an Olympic gold medal winner.
FOL: -NobelPhysicsLaureate(Amy) -> -OlympicGoldMedalWinner(Amy)
TEXT: If Amy is not an Olympic gold medal winner, then Amy is a Nobel physics laureate.
FOL: -OlympicGoldMedalWinner(Amy) -> NobelLaureate(Amy)

ANSWER: False
</EVALUATE>

=== Example 31 ===
Prompt:
The following is a first-order logic (FOL) problem.
The problem is to determine whether the conclusion follows from the premises.
The premises are given in the form of a set of first-order logic sentences.
The conclusion is given in the form of a single first-order logic sentence.
The task is to translate each of the premises and conclusions into FOL expressions.and then to evaluate the conclusion as ANSWER: True, ANSWER: False, or ANSWER: Uncertain given the premises. The output should follow format TEXT: 
FOL: 
TEXT: 
FOL:... ANSWER: 


<PREMISES>
All biodegradable things are environment-friendly.
All woodware is biodegradable.
All paper is woodware.
Nothing is a good thing and also a bad thing.
All environment-friendly things are good.
A worksheet is either paper or environment-friendly.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
A worksheet is not biodegradable.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>
TEXT: All biodegradable things are environment-friendly.
FOL: all x. (Biodegradable(x) -> EnvironmentFriendly(x))
TEXT: All woodware is biodegradable.
FOL: all x. (Woodware(x) -> Biodegradable(x))
TEXT: All paper is woodware.
FOL: all x. (Paper(x) -> Woodware(x))
TEXT: Nothing is a good thing and also a bad thing.
FOL: -(exists x. (Good(x) & Bad(x)))
TEXT: All environment-friendly things are good.
FOL: all x. (EnvironmentFriendly(x) -> Good(x))
TEXT: A worksheet is either paper or environment-friendly.
FOL: ((Paper(Worksheet) & -EnvironmentFriendly(Worksheet)) | (-Paper(Worksheet) & EnvironmentFriendly(Worksheet)))
TEXT: A worksheet is not biodegradable.
FOL: -Dispensable(Worksheet)

ANSWER: Uncertain
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
A La Liga soccer team ranks higher than another La Liga soccer team if it receives more points.
If there are two La Liga soccer teams and neither has more points than the other, then the team which receives more points from the games between the two teams ranks higher.
Real Madrid and Barcelona are both La Liga soccer teams.
Real Madrid received more points than Barcelona.
Neither Real Madrid nor Barcelona received more points from the games between them.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
Real Madrid ranks higher than Barcelona.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>
TEXT: A La Liga soccer team ranks higher than another La Liga soccer team if it receives more points.
FOL: all x. all y. (LaLigaSoccerTeam(x) & LaLigaSoccerTeam(y) & MorePoints(x, y) -> RankHigherThan(x, y))
TEXT: If there are two La Liga soccer teams and neither has more points than the other, then the team which receives more points from the games between the two teams ranks higher.
FOL: all x. all y. (LaLigaSoccerTeam(x) & LaLigaSoccerTeam(y) & -MorePoints(x, y) & -MorePoints(y, x) & MorePointsInGameBetween(x, y) ->  RankHigherThan(x, y))
TEXT: Real Madrid and Barcelona are both La Liga soccer teams.
FOL: LaLigaSoccerTeam(RealMadrid) & LaLigaSoccerTeam(Barcelona)
TEXT: Real Madrid received more points than Barcelona.
FOL: MorePoints(RealMadrid, Barcelona)
TEXT: Neither Real Madrid nor Barcelona received more points from the games between them.
FOL: -MorePointsInGameBetween(RealMadrid, Barcelona) & -MorePointsInGameBetween(Barcelona, RealMadrid)
TEXT: Real Madrid ranks higher than Barcelona.
FOL: HigherRank(RealMadrid, Barcelona)

ANSWER: True
</EVALUATE>

Therefore, by applying the transitivity rule provided in the fourth premise, we can deduce that Ainderby Quernhow, being a civil parish, is located in England. This directly contradicts the conclusion that there is no civil parish in England, making the conclusion false.
Processed: False

Generation 5:
TEXT: Ainderby Quernhow is a village and civil parish in the Hambleton District.
FOL: CivilParish(AinderbyQuernhow) & LocatedIn(AinderbyQuernhow, HambletonDistrict)
TEXT: Hambleton District is in North Yorkshire.
FOL: LocatedIn(HambletonDistrict, NorthYorkshire)
TEXT: North Yorkshire is in England.
FOL: LocatedIn(NorthYorkshire, England)
TEXT: If place A is located in place B and place B is located in place C, then place A is located in place C.
FOL: all A. all B. all C. (LocatedIn(A, B) & LocatedIn(B, C) -> LocatedIn(A, C))
TEXT: There is no civil parish in England.
FOL: -(exists x. CivilParish(x) & LocatedIn(x, England))

ANSWER: False

Explanation: From the premises, we can infer that Ainderby Quernhow, being a civil parish, is located in Hambleton District, which is located in North Yorkshire, and North Yorkshire is located in England. Therefore, by transitivity, Ainderby Quernhow is located in England. This means there is at least one civil parish in England, contradicting the conclusion.
Processed: False

=== Example 33 ===
Prompt:
The following is a first-order logic (FOL) problem.
The problem is to determine whether the conclusion follows from the premises.
The premises are given in the form of a set of first-order logic sentences.
The conclusion is given in the form of a single first-order logic sentence.
The task is to translate each of the premises and conclusions into FOL expressions.and then to evaluate the conclusion as ANSWER: True, ANSWER: False, or ANSWER: Uncertain given the premises. The output should follow format TEXT: 
FOL: 
TEXT: 
FOL:... ANSWER: 


<PREMISES>
All biodegradable things are environment-friendly.
All woodware is biodegradable.
All paper is woodware.
Nothing is a good thing and also a bad thing.
All environment-friendly things are good.
A worksheet is either paper or environment-friendly.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
A worksheet is not biodegradable.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>
TEXT: All biodegradable things are environment-friendly.
FOL: all x. (Biodegradable(x) -> EnvironmentFriendly(x))
TEXT: All woodware is biodegradable.
FOL: all x. (Woodware(x) -> Biodegradable(x))
TEXT: All paper is woodware.
FOL: all x. (Paper(x) -> Woodware(x))
TEXT: Nothing is a good thing and also a bad thing.
FOL: -(exists x. (Good(x) & Bad(x)))
TEXT: All environment-friendly things are good.
FOL: all x. (EnvironmentFriendly(x) -> Good(x))
TEXT: A worksheet is either paper or environment-friendly.
FOL: ((Paper(Worksheet) & -EnvironmentFriendly(Worksheet)) | (-Paper(Worksheet) & EnvironmentFriendly(Worksheet)))
TEXT: A worksheet is not biodegradable.
FOL: -Dispensable(Worksheet)

ANSWER: Uncertain
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
A La Liga soccer team ranks higher than another La Liga soccer team if it receives more points.
If there are two La Liga soccer teams and neither has more points than the other, then the team which receives more points from the games between the two teams ranks higher.
Real Madrid and Barcelona are both La Liga soccer teams.
Real Madrid received more points than Barcelona.
Neither Real Madrid nor Barcelona received more points from the games between them.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
Real Madrid ranks higher than Barcelona.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>
TEXT: A La Liga soccer team ranks higher than another La Liga soccer team if it receives more points.
FOL: all x. all y. (LaLigaSoccerTeam(x) & LaLigaSoccerTeam(y) & MorePoints(x, y) -> RankHigherThan(x, y))
TEXT: If there are two La Liga soccer teams and neither has more points than the other, then the team which receives more points from the games between the two teams ranks higher.
FOL: all x. all y. (LaLigaSoccerTeam(x) & LaLigaSoccerTeam(y) & -MorePoints(x, y) & -MorePoints(y, x) & MorePointsInGameBetween(x, y) ->  RankHigherThan(x, y))
TEXT: Real Madrid and Barcelona are both La Liga soccer teams.
FOL: LaLigaSoccerTeam(RealMadrid) & LaLigaSoccerTeam(Barcelona)
TEXT: Real Madrid received more points than Barcelona.
FOL: MorePoints(RealMadrid, Barcelona)
TEXT: Neither Real Madrid nor Barcelona received more points from the games between them.
FOL: -MorePointsInGameBetween(RealMadrid, Barcelona) & -MorePointsInGameBetween(Barcelona, RealMadrid)
TEXT: Real Madrid ranks higher than Barcelona.
FOL: HigherRank(RealMadrid, Barcelona)

ANSWER: True
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
All professional athletes spend most of their time on sports.
All Olympic gold medal winners are professional athletes.
No full-time scientists spend the majority of their time on sports.
All Nobel physics laureates are full-time scientists.
Amy spends the most time on sports, or Amy is an Olympic gold medal winner.
If Amy is not a Nobel physics laureate, then Amy is not an Olympic gold medal winner.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
If Amy is not an Olympic gold medal winner, then Amy is a Nobel physics laureate.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>
TEXT: All professional athletes spend most of their time on sports.
FOL: all x. (ProfessionalAthlete(x) -> SpendOn(x, MostOfTheirTime, Sports))
TEXT: All Olympic gold medal winners are professional athletes.
FOL: all x. (OlympicGoldMedalWinner(x) -> ProfessionalAthlete(x))
TEXT: No full-time scientists spend the majority of their time on sports.
FOL: all x. (FullTimeScientist(x) -> -SpendOn(x, MostOfTheirTime, Sports))
TEXT: All Nobel physics laureates are full-time scientists.
FOL: all x. (NobelPhysicsLaureate(x) -> FullTimeScientist(x))
TEXT: Amy spends the most time on sports, or Amy is an Olympic gold medal winner.
FOL: SpendOn(Amy, MostOfTheirTime, Sports) | OlympicGoldMedalWinner(Amy)
TEXT: If Amy is not a Nobel physics laureate, then Amy is not an Olympic gold medal winner.
FOL: -NobelPhysicsLaureate(Amy) -> -OlympicGoldMedalWinner(Amy)
TEXT: If Amy is not an Olympic gold medal winner, then Amy is a Nobel physics laureate.
FOL: -OlympicGoldMedalWinner(Amy) -> NobelLaureate(Amy)

ANSWER: False
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
Douglas Adams is an author who created the book collection called The Salmon of Doubt.
The Salmon of Doubt is about life experiences and technology.
All authors are writers.
Writers create innovative ideas.
Some books that contain innovative ideas are about technology.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
Douglas Adams is a writer.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>

=== Example 36 ===
Prompt:
The following is a first-order logic (FOL) problem.
The problem is to determine whether the conclusion follows from the premises.
The premises are given in the form of a set of first-order logic sentences.
The conclusion is given in the form of a single first-order logic sentence.
The task is to translate each of the premises and conclusions into FOL expressions.and then to evaluate the conclusion as ANSWER: True, ANSWER: False, or ANSWER: Uncertain given the premises. The output should follow format TEXT: 
FOL: 
TEXT: 
FOL:... ANSWER: 


<PREMISES>
All biodegradable things are environment-friendly.
All woodware is biodegradable.
All paper is woodware.
Nothing is a good thing and also a bad thing.
All environment-friendly things are good.
A worksheet is either paper or environment-friendly.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
A worksheet is not biodegradable.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>
TEXT: All biodegradable things are environment-friendly.
FOL: all x. (Biodegradable(x) -> EnvironmentFriendly(x))
TEXT: All woodware is biodegradable.
FOL: all x. (Woodware(x) -> Biodegradable(x))
TEXT: All paper is woodware.
FOL: all x. (Paper(x) -> Woodware(x))
TEXT: Nothing is a good thing and also a bad thing.
FOL: -(exists x. (Good(x) & Bad(x)))
TEXT: All environment-friendly things are good.
FOL: all x. (EnvironmentFriendly(x) -> Good(x))
TEXT: A worksheet is either paper or environment-friendly.
FOL: ((Paper(Worksheet) & -EnvironmentFriendly(Worksheet)) | (-Paper(Worksheet) & EnvironmentFriendly(Worksheet)))
TEXT: A worksheet is not biodegradable.
FOL: -Dispensable(Worksheet)

ANSWER: Uncertain
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
A La Liga soccer team ranks higher than another La Liga soccer team if it receives more points.
If there are two La Liga soccer teams and neither has more points than the other, then the team which receives more points from the games between the two teams ranks higher.
Real Madrid and Barcelona are both La Liga soccer teams.
Real Madrid received more points than Barcelona.
Neither Real Madrid nor Barcelona received more points from the games between them.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
Real Madrid ranks higher than Barcelona.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>
TEXT: A La Liga soccer team ranks higher than another La Liga soccer team if it receives more points.
FOL: all x. all y. (LaLigaSoccerTeam(x) & LaLigaSoccerTeam(y) & MorePoints(x, y) -> RankHigherThan(x, y))
TEXT: If there are two La Liga soccer teams and neither has more points than the other, then the team which receives more points from the games between the two teams ranks higher.
FOL: all x. all y. (LaLigaSoccerTeam(x) & LaLigaSoccerTeam(y) & -MorePoints(x, y) & -MorePoints(y, x) & MorePointsInGameBetween(x, y) ->  RankHigherThan(x, y))
TEXT: Real Madrid and Barcelona are both La Liga soccer teams.
FOL: LaLigaSoccerTeam(RealMadrid) & LaLigaSoccerTeam(Barcelona)
TEXT: Real Madrid received more points than Barcelona.
FOL: MorePoints(RealMadrid, Barcelona)
TEXT: Neither Real Madrid nor Barcelona received more points from the games between them.
FOL: -MorePointsInGameBetween(RealMadrid, Barcelona) & -MorePointsInGameBetween(Barcelona, RealMadrid)
TEXT: Real Madrid ranks higher than Barcelona.
FOL: HigherRank(RealMadrid, Barcelona)

ANSWER: True
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
All professional athletes spend most of their time on sports.
All Olympic gold medal winners are professional athletes.
No full-time scientists spend the majority of their time on sports.
All Nobel physics laureates are full-time scientists.
Amy spends the most time on sports, or Amy is an Olympic gold medal winner.
If Amy is not a Nobel physics laureate, then Amy is not an Olympic gold medal winner.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
If Amy is not an Olympic gold medal winner, then Amy is a Nobel physics laureate.
</CONCLUSION>

TEXT: If Amy is not an Olympic gold medal winner, then Amy is a Nobel physics laureate.

ANSWER: False
</EVALUATE>

The premises are given in the form of a set of first-order logic sentences.
The conclusion is given in the form of a single first-order logic sentence.
The task is to translate each of the premises and conclusions into FOL expressions.and then to evaluate the conclusion as ANSWER: True, ANSWER: False, or ANSWER: Uncertain given the premises. The output should follow format TEXT: 
FOL: 
TEXT: 
FOL:... ANSWER: 


<PREMISES>
All biodegradable things are environment-friendly.
All woodware is biodegradable.
All paper is woodware.
Nothing is a good thing and also a bad thing.
All environment-friendly things are good.

</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
A worksheet is not biodegradable.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>
TEXT: All biodegradable things are environment-friendly.
FOL: all x. (Biodegradable(x) -> EnvironmentFriendly(x))
TEXT: All woodware is biodegradable.
FOL: all x. (Woodware(x) -> Biodegradable(x))
TEXT: All paper is woodware.
FOL: all x. (Paper(x) -> Woodware(x))
TEXT: Nothing is a good thing and also a bad thing.
FOL: -(exists x. (Good(x) & Bad(x)))
TEXT: All environment-friendly things are good.
FOL: all x. (EnvironmentFriendly(x) -> Good(x))
TEXT: A worksheet is either paper or environment-friendly.
FOL: ((Paper(Worksheet) & -EnvironmentFriendly(Worksheet)) | (-Paper(Worksheet) & EnvironmentFriendly(Worksheet)))
TEXT: A worksheet is not biodegradable.
FOL: -Dispensable(Worksheet)

ANSWER: Uncertain
</EVALUATE>
