The premises are given in the form of a set of first-order logic sentences.
The conclusion is given in the form of a single first-order logic sentence.
The task is to translate each of the premises and conclusions into FOL expressions.and then to evaluate the conclusion as ANSWER: True, ANSWER: False, or ANSWER: Uncertain given the premises. The output should follow format TEXT: 
FOL: 
TEXT: 
FOL:... ANSWER: 


<PREMISES>
All biodegradable things are environment-friendly.
All woodware is biodegradable.
All paper is woodware.
Nothing is a good thing and also a bad thing.
All environment-friendly things are good.
A worksheet is either paper or environment-friendly.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
A worksheet is not biodegradable.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>
TEXT: All biodegradable things are environment-friendly.
FOL: all x. (Biodegradable(x) -> EnvironmentFriendly(x))
TEXT: All woodware is biodegradable.
FOL: all x. (Woodware(x) -> Biodegradable(x))
TEXT: All paper is woodware.
FOL: all x. (Paper(x) -> Woodware(x))
TEXT: Nothing is a good thing and also a bad thing.
FOL: -(exists x. (Good(x) & Bad(x)))
TEXT: All environment-friendly things are good.
FOL: all x. (EnvironmentFriendly(x) -> Good(x))
TEXT: A worksheet is either paper or environment-friendly.
FOL: ((Paper(Worksheet) & -EnvironmentFriendly(Worksheet)) | (-Paper(Worksheet) & EnvironmentFriendly(Worksheet)))
TEXT: A worksheet is not biodegradable.
FOL: -Dispensable(Worksheet)

ANSWER: Uncertain
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
A La Liga soccer team ranks higher than another La Liga soccer team if it receives more points.
If there are two La Liga soccer teams and neither has more points than the other, then the team which receives more points from the games between the two teams ranks higher.
Real Madrid and Barcelona are both La Liga soccer teams.
Real Madrid received more points than Barcelona.
Neither Real Madrid nor Barcelona received more points from the games between them.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
Real Madrid ranks higher than Barcelona.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>
TEXT: A La Liga soccer team ranks higher than another La Liga soccer team if it receives more points.
FOL: all x. all y. (LaLigaSoccerTeam(x) & LaLigaSoccerTeam(y) & MorePoints(x, y) -> RankHigherThan(x, y))
TEXT: If there are two La Liga soccer teams and neither has more points than the other, then the team which receives more points from the games between the two teams ranks higher.
FOL: all x. all y. (LaLigaSoccerTeam(x) & LaLigaSoccerTeam(y) & -MorePoints(x, y) & -MorePoints(y, x) & MorePointsInGameBetween(x, y) ->  RankHigherThan(x, y))
TEXT: Real Madrid and Barcelona are both La Liga soccer teams.
FOL: LaLigaSoccerTeam(RealMadrid) & LaLigaSoccerTeam(Barcelona)
TEXT: Real Madrid received more points than Barcelona.
FOL: MorePoints(RealMadrid, Barcelona)
TEXT: Neither Real Madrid nor Barcelona received more points from the games between them.
FOL: -MorePointsInGameBetween(RealMadrid, Barcelona) & -MorePointsInGameBetween(Barcelona, RealMadrid)
TEXT: Real Madrid ranks higher than Barcelona.
FOL: HigherRank(RealMadrid, Barcelona)

ANSWER: True
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
All professional athletes spend most of their time on sports.
All Olympic gold medal winners are professional athletes.
No full-time scientists spend the majority of their time on sports.
All Nobel physics laureates are full-time scientists.
Amy spends the most time on sports, or Amy is an Olympic gold medal winner.
If Amy is not a Nobel physics laureate, then Amy is not an Olympic gold medal winner.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
If Amy is not an Olympic gold medal winner, then Amy is a Nobel physics laureate.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>
TEXT: All professional athletes spend most of their time on sports.
FOL: all x. (ProfessionalAthlete(x) -> SpendOn(x, MostOfTheirTime, Sports))
TEXT: All Olympic gold medal winners are professional athletes.
FOL: all x. (OlympicGoldMedalWinner(x) -> ProfessionalAthlete(x))
TEXT: No full-time scientists spend the majority of their time on sports.
FOL: all x. (FullTimeScientist(x) -> -SpendOn(x, MostOfTheirTime, Sports))
TEXT: All Nobel physics laureates are full-time scientists.
FOL: all x. (NobelPhysicsLaureate(x) -> FullTimeScientist(x))
TEXT: Amy spends the most time on sports, or Amy is an Olympic gold medal winner.
FOL: SpendOn(Amy, MostOfTheirTime, Sports) | OlympicGoldMedalWinner(Amy)
TEXT: If Amy is not a Nobel physics laureate, then Amy is not an Olympic gold medal winner.
FOL: -NobelPhysicsLaureate(Amy) -> -OlympicGoldMedalWinner(Amy)
TEXT: If Amy is not an Olympic gold medal winner, then Amy is a Nobel physics laureate.
FOL: -OlympicGoldMedalWinner(Amy) -> NobelLaureate(Amy)

ANSWER: False
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
China is one of the BRICS, and its economy is emerging.
If someone is from China, then they are from a country of BRICS.
India is one of the BRICS, and its economy is emerging.
If someone is from India, then they are in a country of BRICS.
All people from China are Chinese people.
All people from India are Indian people.
There is a person from India.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
No people from BRICS are Indian people.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>

Generation 1:
TEXT: China is one of the BRICS, and its economy is emerging.
FOL: BRICS(China) & EconomyEmerging(China)
TEXT: If someone is from China, then they are from a country of BRICS.
FOL: all x. (From(x, China) -> FromCountryOfBRICS(x))
TEXT: India is one of the BRICS, and its economy is emerging.
FOL: BRICS(India) & EconomyEmerging(India)
TEXT: If someone is from India, then they are in a country of BRICS.
FOL: all x. (From(x, India) -> FromCountryOfBRICS(x))
TEXT: All people from China are Chinese people.
FOL: all x. (From(x, China) -> ChinesePeople(x))
TEXT: All people from India are Indian people.
FOL: all x. (From(x, India) -> IndianPeople(x))
TEXT: There is a person from India.
FOL: exists x. From(x, India)
TEXT: No people from BRICS are Indian people.
FOL: -exists x. (FromCountryOfBRICS(x) & IndianPeople(x))

ANSWER: False

Explanation:
Given that India is part of BRICS and all people from India are Indian people, it contradicts the conclusion. Since there is a person from India (and thus an Indian person from a BRICS country), the statement "No people from BRICS are Indian people" cannot be true according to the premises provided. Therefore, the answer is False.
Processed: False

TEXT: China is one of the BRICS, and its economy is emerging.
FOL: BRICS(China) & EconomyEmerging(China)
TEXT: If someone is from China, then they are from a country of BRICS.
FOL: all x. (From(x, China) -> FromCountryBRICS(x))

ANSWER: False

Explanation:
Given that India is part of the BRICS and anyone from India is considered from a BRICS country (FromCountryBRICS), and considering there is at least one person from India (From(x, India)), it implies that this person from India would be both from a BRICS country and an Indian person, thus contradicting the conclusion "No people from BRICS are Indian people." Therefore, the conclusion does not follow from the premises and is evaluated as False.

=== Example 46 ===
Prompt:
The following is a first-order logic (FOL) problem.
The problem is to determine whether the conclusion follows from the premises.
The premises are given in the form of a set of first-order logic sentences.
The conclusion is given in the form of a single first-order logic sentence.
The task is to translate each of the premises and conclusions into FOL expressions.and then to evaluate the conclusion as ANSWER: True, ANSWER: False, or ANSWER: Uncertain given the premises. The output should follow format TEXT: 
FOL: 
TEXT: 
FOL:... ANSWER: 


<PREMISES>
All biodegradable things are environment-friendly.
All woodware is biodegradable.
All paper is woodware.
Nothing is a good thing and also a bad thing.
All environment-friendly things are good.
A worksheet is either paper or environment-friendly.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
A worksheet is not biodegradable.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>
TEXT: All biodegradable things are environment-friendly.
FOL: all x. (Biodegradable(x) -> EnvironmentFriendly(x))
TEXT: All woodware is biodegradable.
FOL: all x. (Woodware(x) -> Biodegradable(x))
TEXT: All paper is woodware.
FOL: all x. (Paper(x) -> Woodware(x))
TEXT: Nothing is a good thing and also a bad thing.
FOL: -(exists x. (Good(x) & Bad(x)))
TEXT: All environment-friendly things are good.
FOL: all x. (EnvironmentFriendly(x) -> Good(x))
TEXT: A worksheet is either paper or environment-friendly.
FOL: ((Paper(Worksheet) & -EnvironmentFriendly(Worksheet)) | (-Paper(Worksheet) & EnvironmentFriendly(Worksheet)))
TEXT: A worksheet is not biodegradable.
FOL: -Dispensable(Worksheet)

ANSWER: Uncertain
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
A La Liga soccer team ranks higher than another La Liga soccer team if it receives more points.
If there are two La Liga soccer teams and neither has more points than the other, then the team which receives more points from the games between the two teams ranks higher.
Real Madrid and Barcelona are both La Liga soccer teams.
Real Madrid received more points than Barcelona.
Neither Real Madrid nor Barcelona received more points from the games between them.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
Real Madrid ranks higher than Barcelona.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>
TEXT: A La Liga soccer team ranks higher than another La Liga soccer team if it receives more points.
FOL: all x. all y. (LaLigaSoccerTeam(x) & LaLigaSoccerTeam(y) & MorePoints(x, y) -> RankHigherThan(x, y))
TEXT: If there are two La Liga soccer teams and neither has more points than the other, then the team which receives more points from the games between the two teams ranks higher.
FOL: all x. all y. (LaLigaSoccerTeam(x) & LaLigaSoccerTeam(y) & -MorePoints(x, y) & -MorePoints(y, x) & MorePointsInGameBetween(x, y) ->  RankHigherThan(x, y))
TEXT: Real Madrid and Barcelona are both La Liga soccer teams.
FOL: LaLigaSoccerTeam(RealMadrid) & LaLigaSoccerTeam(Barcelona)
TEXT: Real Madrid received more points than Barcelona.
FOL: MorePoints(RealMadrid, Barcelona)
TEXT: Neither Real Madrid nor Barcelona received more points from the games between them.
FOL: -MorePointsInGameBetween(RealMadrid, Barcelona) & -MorePointsInGameBetween(Barcelona, RealMadrid)
TEXT: Real Madrid ranks higher than Barcelona.
FOL: HigherRank(RealMadrid, Barcelona)

ANSWER: True
</EVALUATE>

If Amy is not a Nobel physics laureate, then Amy is not an Olympic gold medal winner.

<CONCLUSION>

=== Example 48 ===
Prompt:
The following is a first-order logic (FOL) problem.
The problem is to determine whether the conclusion follows from the premises.
The premises are given in the form of a set of first-order logic sentences.
The conclusion is given in the form of a single first-order logic sentence.
The task is to translate each of the premises and conclusions into FOL expressions.and then to evaluate the conclusion as ANSWER: True, ANSWER: False, or ANSWER: Uncertain given the premises. The output should follow format TEXT: 
FOL: 
TEXT: 
FOL:... ANSWER: 


<PREMISES>
All biodegradable things are environment-friendly.
All woodware is biodegradable.
All paper is woodware.
Nothing is a good thing and also a bad thing.
All environment-friendly things are good.
A worksheet is either paper or environment-friendly.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
A worksheet is not biodegradable.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>
TEXT: All biodegradable things are environment-friendly.
FOL: all x. (Biodegradable(x) -> EnvironmentFriendly(x))
TEXT: All woodware is biodegradable.
FOL: all x. (Woodware(x) -> Biodegradable(x))
TEXT: All paper is woodware.
FOL: all x. (Paper(x) -> Woodware(x))
TEXT: Nothing is a good thing and also a bad thing.
FOL: -(exists x. (Good(x) & Bad(x)))
TEXT: All environment-friendly things are good.
FOL: all x. (EnvironmentFriendly(x) -> Good(x))
TEXT: A worksheet is either paper or environment-friendly.
FOL: ((Paper(Worksheet) & -EnvironmentFriendly(Worksheet)) | (-Paper(Worksheet) & EnvironmentFriendly(Worksheet)))
TEXT: A worksheet is not biodegradable.
FOL: -Dispensable(Worksheet)

ANSWER: Uncertain
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
A La Liga soccer team ranks higher than another La Liga soccer team if it receives more points.
If there are two La Liga soccer teams and neither has more points than the other, then the team which receives more points from the games between the two teams ranks higher.
Real Madrid and Barcelona are both La Liga soccer teams.
Real Madrid received more points than Barcelona.
Neither Real Madrid nor Barcelona received more points from the games between them.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
Real Madrid ranks higher than Barcelona.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>
TEXT: A La Liga soccer team ranks higher than another La Liga soccer team if it receives more points.
FOL: all x. all y. (LaLigaSoccerTeam(x) & LaLigaSoccerTeam(y) & MorePoints(x, y) -> RankHigherThan(x, y))
TEXT: If there are two La Liga soccer teams and neither has more points than the other, then the team which receives more points from the games between the two teams ranks higher.
FOL: all x. all y. (LaLigaSoccerTeam(x) & LaLigaSoccerTeam(y) & -MorePoints(x, y) & -MorePoints(y, x) & MorePointsInGameBetween(x, y) ->  RankHigherThan(x, y))
TEXT: Real Madrid and Barcelona are both La Liga soccer teams.
FOL: LaLigaSoccerTeam(RealMadrid) & LaLigaSoccerTeam(Barcelona)
TEXT: Real Madrid received more points than Barcelona.
FOL: MorePoints(RealMadrid, Barcelona)
TEXT: Neither Real Madrid nor Barcelona received more points from the games between them.
FOL: -MorePointsInGameBetween(RealMadrid, Barcelona) & -MorePointsInGameBetween(Barcelona, RealMadrid)
TEXT: Real Madrid ranks higher than Barcelona.
FOL: HigherRank(RealMadrid, Barcelona)

ANSWER: True
</EVALUATE>

=== Example 50 ===
Prompt:
The following is a first-order logic (FOL) problem.
The problem is to determine whether the conclusion follows from the premises.
The premises are given in the form of a set of first-order logic sentences.
The conclusion is given in the form of a single first-order logic sentence.
The task is to translate each of the premises and conclusions into FOL expressions.and then to evaluate the conclusion as ANSWER: True, ANSWER: False, or ANSWER: Uncertain given the premises. The output should follow format TEXT: 
FOL: 
TEXT: 
FOL:... ANSWER: 


<PREMISES>
All biodegradable things are environment-friendly.
All woodware is biodegradable.
All paper is woodware.
Nothing is a good thing and also a bad thing.
All environment-friendly things are good.
A worksheet is either paper or environment-friendly.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
A worksheet is not biodegradable.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>
TEXT: All biodegradable things are environment-friendly.
FOL: all x. (Biodegradable(x) -> EnvironmentFriendly(x))
TEXT: All woodware is biodegradable.
FOL: all x. (Woodware(x) -> Biodegradable(x))
TEXT: All paper is woodware.
FOL: all x. (Paper(x) -> Woodware(x))
TEXT: Nothing is a good thing and also a bad thing.
FOL: -(exists x. (Good(x) & Bad(x)))
TEXT: All environment-friendly things are good.
FOL: all x. (EnvironmentFriendly(x) -> Good(x))
TEXT: A worksheet is either paper or environment-friendly.
FOL: ((Paper(Worksheet) & -EnvironmentFriendly(Worksheet)) | (-Paper(Worksheet) & EnvironmentFriendly(Worksheet)))
TEXT: A worksheet is not biodegradable.
FOL: -Dispensable(Worksheet)

ANSWER: Uncertain
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
A La Liga soccer team ranks higher than another La Liga soccer team if it receives more points.
If there are two La Liga soccer teams and neither has more points than the other, then the team which receives more points from the games between the two teams ranks higher.
Real Madrid and Barcelona are both La Liga soccer teams.
Real Madrid received more points than Barcelona.
Neither Real Madrid nor Barcelona received more points from the games between them.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
Real Madrid ranks higher than Barcelona.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>
TEXT: A La Liga soccer team ranks higher than another La Liga soccer team if it receives more points.
FOL: all x. all y. (LaLigaSoccerTeam(x) & LaLigaSoccerTeam(y) & MorePoints(x, y) -> RankHigherThan(x, y))
TEXT: If there are two La Liga soccer teams and neither has more points than the other, then the team which receives more points from the games between the two teams ranks higher.
FOL: all x. all y. (LaLigaSoccerTeam(x) & LaLigaSoccerTeam(y) & -MorePoints(x, y) & -MorePoints(y, x) & MorePointsInGameBetween(x, y) ->  RankHigherThan(x, y))
TEXT: Real Madrid and Barcelona are both La Liga soccer teams.
FOL: LaLigaSoccerTeam(RealMadrid) & LaLigaSoccerTeam(Barcelona)
TEXT: Real Madrid received more points than Barcelona.
FOL: MorePoints(RealMadrid, Barcelona)
TEXT: Neither Real Madrid nor Barcelona received more points from the games between them.
FOL: -MorePointsInGameBetween(RealMadrid, Barcelona) & -MorePointsInGameBetween(Barcelona, RealMadrid)
TEXT: Real Madrid ranks higher than Barcelona.
FOL: HigherRank(RealMadrid, Barcelona)

ANSWER: True
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
All professional athletes spend most of their time on sports.
All Olympic gold medal winners are professional athletes.
No full-time scientists spend the majority of their time on sports.
All Nobel physics laureates are full-time scientists.
Amy spends the most time on sports, or Amy is an Olympic gold medal winner.
If Amy is not a Nobel physics laureate, then Amy is not an Olympic gold medal winner.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
If Amy is not an Olympic gold medal winner, then Amy is a Nobel physics laureate.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>
TEXT: All professional athletes spend most of their time on sports.
FOL: all x. (ProfessionalAthlete(x) -> SpendOn(x, MostOfTheirTime, Sports))
TEXT: All Olympic gold medal winners are professional athletes.
FOL: all x. (OlympicGoldMedalWinner(x) -> ProfessionalAthlete(x))
TEXT: No full-time scientists spend the majority of their time on sports.
FOL: all x. (FullTimeScientist(x) -> -SpendOn(x, MostOfTheirTime, Sports))
TEXT: All Nobel physics laureates are full-time scientists.
FOL: all x. (NobelPhysicsLaureate(x) -> FullTimeScientist(x))
TEXT: Amy spends the most time on sports, or Amy is an Olympic gold medal winner.
FOL: SpendOn(Amy, MostOfTheirTime, Sports) | OlympicGoldMedalWinner(Amy)
TEXT: If Amy is not a Nobel physics laureate, then Amy is not an Olympic gold medal winner.
FOL: -NobelPhysicsLaureate(Amy) -> -OlympicGoldMedalWinner(Amy)
TEXT: If Amy is not an Olympic gold medal winner, then Amy is a Nobel physics laureate.
FOL: -OlympicGoldMedalWinner(Amy) -> NobelLaureate(Amy)

ANSWER: False
</EVALUATE>

The conclusion is given in the form of a single first-order logic sentence.
The task is to translate each of the premises and conclusions into FOL expressions.and then to evaluate the conclusion as ANSWER: True, ANSWER: False, or ANSWER: Uncertain given the premises. The output should follow format TEXT: 
FOL: 
TEXT: 
FOL:... ANSWER: 


<PREMISES>
All biodegradable things are environment-friendly.
All woodware is biodegradable.
All paper is woodware.
Nothing is a good thing and also a bad thing.
All environment-friendly things are good.
A worksheet is either paper or environment-friendly.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
A worksheet is not biodegradable.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>
TEXT: All biodegradable things are environment-friendly.
FOL: all x. (Biodegradable(x) -> EnvironmentFriendly(x))
TEXT: All woodware is biodegradable.
FOL: all x. (Woodware(x) -> Biodegradable(x))
TEXT: All paper is woodware.
FOL: all x. (Paper(x) -> Woodware(x))
TEXT: Nothing is a good thing and also a bad thing.
FOL: -(exists x. (Good(x) & Bad(x)))
TEXT: All environment-friendly things are good.
FOL: all x. (EnvironmentFriendly(x) -> Good(x))
TEXT: A worksheet is either paper or environment-friendly.
FOL: ((Paper(Worksheet) & -EnvironmentFriendly(Worksheet)) | (-Paper(Worksheet) & EnvironmentFriendly(Worksheet)))
TEXT: A worksheet is not biodegradable.
FOL: -Dispensable(Worksheet)

ANSWER: Uncertain
</EVALUATE>

=== Example 58 ===
Prompt:
The following is a first-order logic (FOL) problem.
The problem is to determine whether the conclusion follows from the premises.
The premises are given in the form of a set of first-order logic sentences.
The conclusion is given in the form of a single first-order logic sentence.
The task is to translate each of the premises and conclusions into FOL expressions.and then to evaluate the conclusion as ANSWER: True, ANSWER: False, or ANSWER: Uncertain given the premises. The output should follow format TEXT: 
FOL: 
TEXT: 
FOL:... ANSWER: 


<PREMISES>
All biodegradable things are environment-friendly.
All woodware is biodegradable.
All paper is woodware.
Nothing is a good thing and also a bad thing.
All environment-friendly things are good.
A worksheet is either paper or environment-friendly.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
A worksheet is not biodegradable.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>
TEXT: All biodegradable things are environment-friendly.
FOL: all x. (Biodegradable(x) -> EnvironmentFriendly(x))
TEXT: All woodware is biodegradable.
FOL: all x. (Woodware(x) -> Biodegradable(x))
TEXT: All paper is woodware.
FOL: all x. (Paper(x) -> Woodware(x))
TEXT: Nothing is a good thing and also a bad thing.
FOL: -(exists x. (Good(x) & Bad(x)))
TEXT: All environment-friendly things are good.
FOL: all x. (EnvironmentFriendly(x) -> Good(x))
TEXT: A worksheet is either paper or environment-friendly.
FOL: ((Paper(Worksheet) & -EnvironmentFriendly(Worksheet)) | (-Paper(Worksheet) & EnvironmentFriendly(Worksheet)))
TEXT: A worksheet is not biodegradable.
FOL: -Dispensable(Worksheet)

ANSWER: Uncertain
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
A La Liga soccer team ranks higher than another La Liga soccer team if it receives more points.
If there are two La Liga soccer teams and neither has more points than the other, then the team which receives more points from the games between the two teams ranks higher.
Real Madrid and Barcelona are both La Liga soccer teams.
Real Madrid received more points than Barcelona.
Neither Real Madrid nor Barcelona received more points from the games between them.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
Real Madrid ranks higher than Barcelona.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>
TEXT: A La Liga soccer team ranks higher than another La Liga soccer team if it receives more points.
FOL: all x. all y. (LaLigaSoccerTeam(x) & LaLigaSoccerTeam(y) & MorePoints(x, y) -> RankHigherThan(x, y))
TEXT: If there are two La Liga soccer teams and neither has more points than the other, then the team which receives more points from the games between the two teams ranks higher.
FOL: all x. all y. (LaLigaSoccerTeam(x) & LaLigaSoccerTeam(y) & -MorePoints(x, y) & -MorePoints(y, x) & MorePointsInGameBetween(x, y) ->  RankHigherThan(x, y))
TEXT: Real Madrid and Barcelona are both La Liga soccer teams.
FOL: LaLigaSoccerTeam(RealMadrid) & LaLigaSoccerTeam(Barcelona)
TEXT: Real Madrid received more points than Barcelona.
FOL: MorePoints(RealMadrid, Barcelona)
TEXT: Neither Real Madrid nor Barcelona received more points from the games between them.
FOL: -MorePointsInGameBetween(RealMadrid, Barcelona) & -MorePointsInGameBetween(Barcelona, RealMadrid)
TEXT: Real Madrid ranks higher than Barcelona.
FOL: HigherRank(RealMadrid, Barcelona)

ANSWER: True
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
All professional athletes spend most of their time on sports.
All Olympic gold medal winners are professional athletes.
No full-time scientists spend the majority of their time on sports.
All Nobel physics laureates are full-time scientists.
Amy spends the most time on sports, or Amy is an Olympic gold medal winner.
If Amy is not a Nobel physics laureate, then Amy is not an Olympic gold medal winner.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
If Amy is not an Olympic gold medal winner, then Amy is a Nobel physics laureate.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>
TEXT: All professional athletes spend most of their time on sports.
FOL: all x. (ProfessionalAthlete(x) -> SpendOn(x, MostOfTheirTime, Sports))
TEXT: All Olympic gold medal winners are professional athletes.
FOL: all x. (OlympicGoldMedalWinner(x) -> ProfessionalAthlete(x))
TEXT: No full-time scientists spend the majority of their time on sports.
FOL: all x. (FullTimeScientist(x) -> -SpendOn(x, MostOfTheirTime, Sports))
TEXT: All Nobel physics laureates are full-time scientists.
FOL: all x. (NobelPhysicsLaureate(x) -> FullTimeScientist(x))
TEXT: Amy spends the most time on sports, or Amy is an Olympic gold medal winner.
FOL: SpendOn(Amy, MostOfTheirTime, Sports) | OlympicGoldMedalWinner(Amy)
TEXT: If Amy is not a Nobel physics laureate, then Amy is not an Olympic gold medal winner.
FOL: -NobelPhysicsLaureate(Amy) -> -OlympicGoldMedalWinner(Amy)
TEXT: If Amy is not an Olympic gold medal winner, then Amy is a Nobel physics laureate.
FOL: -OlympicGoldMedalWinner(Amy) -> NobelLaureate(Amy)

ANSWER: False
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
Tyga is a rapper.
Rappers release rap albums.
Tyga released the Well Done 3 album.
Rappers are not opera singers.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
Tyga is an opera singer.

Explanation: Given the premises, we know that Tyga is a rapper (Rapper(Tyga)), and since all rappers are not opera singers (all x. (Rapper(x) -> -OperaSinger(x))), it follows that Tyga cannot be an opera singer. Therefore, the conclusion that Tyga is an opera singer is false based on the given premises.

<PREMISES>
When the Monkeypox virus occurs in a being, it may get Monkeypox.
Monkeypox virus can occur in certain animals.
Humans are mammals.
Mammals are animals.
Symptoms of Monkeypox include fever, headache, muscle pains, and tiredness.
People feel tired when they get the flu.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
There is an animal.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>

Generation 1:
TEXT: When the Monkeypox virus occurs in a being, it may get Monkeypox.
FOL: all x. (Occur(MonkeypoxVirus, x) -> MayGet(x, Monkeypox))
TEXT: Monkeypox virus can occur in certain animals.
FOL: exists x. (Animal(x) & Occur(MonkeypoxVirus, x))
TEXT: Humans are mammals.
FOL: all x. (Human(x) -> Mammal(x))
TEXT: Mammals are animals.
FOL: all x. (Mammal(x) -> Animal(x))
TEXT: Symptoms of Monkeypox include fever, headache, muscle pains, and tiredness.
FOL: all x. (HaveSymptoms(x, Monkeypox) -> (HasSymptom(x, Fever) & HasSymptom(x, Headache) & HasSymptom(x, MusclePains) & HasSymptom(x, Tiredness)))
TEXT: People feel tired when they get the flu.
FOL: all x. (Person(x) & GetFlu(x) -> FeelTired(x))
TEXT: There is an animal.
FOL: exists x. Animal(x)

ANSWER: True

Explanation:
Given the premise "Monkeypox virus can occur in certain animals," we have the existence of at least one animal in which the Monkeypox virus can occur. Thus, it logically follows that "there is an animal." Therefore, the conclusion "There is an animal" is true given the premises.
Processed: True

=== Example 61 ===
Prompt:
The following is a first-order logic (FOL) problem.
The problem is to determine whether the conclusion follows from the premises.
The premises are given in the form of a set of first-order logic sentences.
The conclusion is given in the form of a single first-order logic sentence.
The task is to translate each of the premises and conclusions into FOL expressions.and then to evaluate the conclusion as ANSWER: True, ANSWER: False, or ANSWER: Uncertain given the premises. The output should follow format TEXT: 
FOL: 
TEXT: 
FOL:... ANSWER: 


<PREMISES>
All biodegradable things are environment-friendly.
All woodware is biodegradable.
All paper is woodware.
Nothing is a good thing and also a bad thing.
All environment-friendly things are good.
A worksheet is either paper or environment-friendly.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
A worksheet is not biodegradable.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>
TEXT: All biodegradable things are environment-friendly.
FOL: all x. (Biodegradable(x) -> EnvironmentFriendly(x))
TEXT: All woodware is biodegradable.
FOL: all x. (Woodware(x) -> Biodegradable(x))
TEXT: All paper is woodware.
FOL: all x. (Paper(x) -> Woodware(x))
TEXT: Nothing is a good thing and also a bad thing.
FOL: -(exists x. (Good(x) & Bad(x)))
TEXT: All environment-friendly things are good.
FOL: all x. (EnvironmentFriendly(x) -> Good(x))
TEXT: A worksheet is either paper or environment-friendly.
FOL: ((Paper(Worksheet) & -EnvironmentFriendly(Worksheet)) | (-Paper(Worksheet) & EnvironmentFriendly(Worksheet)))
TEXT: A worksheet is not biodegradable.
FOL: -Dispensable(Worksheet)

ANSWER: Uncertain
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
A La Liga soccer team ranks higher than another La Liga soccer team if it receives more points.
If there are two La Liga soccer teams and neither has more points than the other, then the team which receives more points from the games between the two teams ranks higher.
Real Madrid and Barcelona are both La Liga soccer teams.
Real Madrid received more points than Barcelona.
Neither Real Madrid nor Barcelona received more points from the games between them.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
Real Madrid ranks higher than Barcelona.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>
TEXT: A La Liga soccer team ranks higher than another La Liga soccer team if it receives more points.
FOL: all x. all y. (LaLigaSoccerTeam(x) & LaLigaSoccerTeam(y) & MorePoints(x, y) -> RankHigherThan(x, y))
TEXT: If there are two La Liga soccer teams and neither has more points than the other, then the team which receives more points from the games between the two teams ranks higher.
FOL: all x. all y. (LaLigaSoccerTeam(x) & LaLigaSoccerTeam(y) & -MorePoints(x, y) & -MorePoints(y, x) & MorePointsInGameBetween(x, y) ->  RankHigherThan(x, y))
TEXT: Real Madrid and Barcelona are both La Liga soccer teams.
FOL: LaLigaSoccerTeam(RealMadrid) & LaLigaSoccerTeam(Barcelona)
TEXT: Real Madrid received more points than Barcelona.
FOL: MorePoints(RealMadrid, Barcelona)
TEXT: Neither Real Madrid nor Barcelona received more points from the games between them.
FOL: -MorePointsInGameBetween(RealMadrid, Barcelona) & -MorePointsInGameBetween(Barcelona, RealMadrid)
TEXT: Real Madrid ranks higher than Barcelona.
FOL: HigherRank(RealMadrid, Barcelona)

ANSWER: True
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
All professional athletes spend most of their time on sports.
All Olympic gold medal winners are professional athletes.
No full-time scientists spend the majority of their time on sports.
All Nobel physics laureates are full-time scientists.

If there are two La Liga soccer teams and neither has more points than the other, then the team which receives more points from the games between the two teams ranks higher.
Real Madrid and Barcelona are both La Liga soccer teams.
Real Madrid received more points than Barcelona.
Neither Real Madrid nor Barcelona received more points from the games between them.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
Real Madrid ranks higher than Barcelona.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>
TEXT: A La Liga soccer team ranks higher than another La Liga soccer team if it receives more points.
FOL: all x. all y. (LaLigaSoccerTeam(x) & LaLigaSoccerTeam(y) & MorePoints(x, y) -> RankHigherThan(x, y))
TEXT: If there are two La Liga soccer teams and neither has more points than the other, then the team which receives more points from the games between the two teams ranks higher.
FOL: all x. all y. (LaLigaSoccerTeam(x) & LaLigaSoccerTeam(y) & -MorePoints(x, y) & -MorePoints(y, x) & MorePointsInGameBetween(x, y) ->  RankHigherThan(x, y))
TEXT: Real Madrid and Barcelona are both La Liga soccer teams.
FOL: LaLigaSoccerTeam(RealMadrid) & LaLigaSoccerTeam(Barcelona)
TEXT: Real Madrid received more points than Barcelona.
FOL: MorePoints(RealMadrid, Barcelona)
TEXT: Neither Real Madrid nor Barcelona received more points from the games between them.
FOL: -MorePointsInGameBetween(RealMadrid, Barcelona) & -MorePointsInGameBetween(Barcelona, RealMadrid)
TEXT: Real Madrid ranks higher than Barcelona.
FOL: HigherRank(RealMadrid, Barcelona)

ANSWER: True
</EVALUATE>

=== Example 64 ===
Prompt:
The following is a first-order logic (FOL) problem.
The problem is to determine whether the conclusion follows from the premises.
The premises are given in the form of a set of first-order logic sentences.
The conclusion is given in the form of a single first-order logic sentence.
The task is to translate each of the premises and conclusions into FOL expressions.and then to evaluate the conclusion as ANSWER: True, ANSWER: False, or ANSWER: Uncertain given the premises. The output should follow format TEXT: 
FOL: 
TEXT: 
FOL:... ANSWER: 


<PREMISES>
All biodegradable things are environment-friendly.
All woodware is biodegradable.
All paper is woodware.
Nothing is a good thing and also a bad thing.
All environment-friendly things are good.
A worksheet is either paper or environment-friendly.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
A worksheet is not biodegradable.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>
TEXT: All biodegradable things are environment-friendly.
FOL: all x. (Biodegradable(x) -> EnvironmentFriendly(x))
TEXT: All woodware is biodegradable.
FOL: all x. (Woodware(x) -> Biodegradable(x))
TEXT: All paper is woodware.
FOL: all x. (Paper(x) -> Woodware(x))
TEXT: Nothing is a good thing and also a bad thing.
FOL: -(exists x. (Good(x) & Bad(x)))
TEXT: All environment-friendly things are good.
FOL: all x. (EnvironmentFriendly(x) -> Good(x))
TEXT: A worksheet is either paper or environment-friendly.
FOL: ((Paper(Worksheet) & -EnvironmentFriendly(Worksheet)) | (-Paper(Worksheet) & EnvironmentFriendly(Worksheet)))
TEXT: A worksheet is not biodegradable.
FOL: -Dispensable(Worksheet)

ANSWER: Uncertain
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
New York City is Located in the United States of America.
The United States of America is part of North America.
North America is in the western hemisphere of the earth.
New York City is a highly developed city.
If place A is located in place B and place B is located in place C, then place A is located in place C.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
The United States of America is not located in the western hemisphere of the earth.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>

Generation 1:
TEXT: New York City is Located in the United States of America.
FOL: Located(NewYorkCity, USA)
TEXT: The United States of America is part of North America.
FOL: PartOf(USA, NorthAmerica)
TEXT: North America is in the western hemisphere of the earth.
FOL: Located(NorthAmerica, WesternHemisphere)
TEXT: New York City is a highly developed city.
FOL: HighlyDeveloped(NewYorkCity)
TEXT: If place A is located in place B and place B is located in place C, then place A is located in place C.
FOL: all A. all B. all C. (Located(A, B) & Located(B, C) -> Located(A, C))

TEXT: The United States of America is not located in the western hemisphere of the earth.
FOL: -Located(USA, WesternHemisphere)

ANSWER: False

Explanation:
From the premises, we can infer that since the United States of America is part of North America (PartOf(USA, NorthAmerica)) and North America is located in the western hemisphere (Located(NorthAmerica, WesternHemisphere)), according to the transitive relationship stated in one of the premises, the United States of America must be located in the western hemisphere (Located(USA, WesternHemisphere)). Therefore, the conclusion stating that the United States of America is not located in the western hemisphere is false.
Processed: False

The only types of mammals that lay eggs are either platypuses or echidnas.

All animals are either vertebrates or invertebrates.
Mammals are animals.

TEXT: The only types of mammals that lay eggs are either platypuses or echidnas.
FOL: all x. (Mammal(x) & LaysEggs(x) -> (Platypus(x) | Echidna(x)))

TEXT: Grebes are not platypuses and also not echidnas.
FOL: -Platypus(Grebes) & -Echidna(Grebes)
TEXT: Grebes are not mammals.
FOL: -Mammal(Grebes)

ANSWER: True

Explanation: Given the premises, grebes laying eggs and not being platypuses or echidnas means they do not fit into the category of egg-laying mammals, which according to the premises, are limited to platypuses and echidnas. Since grebes lay eggs but cannot be categorized under platypuses or echidnas, and considering all mammals are either vertebrates or invertebrates with no mammals being invertebrates, the conclusion that grebes are not mammals logically follows from the premises.

=== Example 66 ===
Prompt:
The following is a first-order logic (FOL) problem.
The problem is to determine whether the conclusion follows from the premises.
The premises are given in the form of a set of first-order logic sentences.
The conclusion is given in the form of a single first-order logic sentence.
The task is to translate each of the premises and conclusions into FOL expressions.and then to evaluate the conclusion as ANSWER: True, ANSWER: False, or ANSWER: Uncertain given the premises. The output should follow format TEXT: 
FOL: 
TEXT: 
FOL:... ANSWER: 


<PREMISES>
All biodegradable things are environment-friendly.
All woodware is biodegradable.
All paper is woodware.
Nothing is a good thing and also a bad thing.
All environment-friendly things are good.
A worksheet is either paper or environment-friendly.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
A worksheet is not biodegradable.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>
TEXT: All biodegradable things are environment-friendly.
FOL: all x. (Biodegradable(x) -> EnvironmentFriendly(x))
TEXT: All woodware is biodegradable.
FOL: all x. (Woodware(x) -> Biodegradable(x))
TEXT: All paper is woodware.
FOL: all x. (Paper(x) -> Woodware(x))
TEXT: Nothing is a good thing and also a bad thing.
FOL: -(exists x. (Good(x) & Bad(x)))
TEXT: All environment-friendly things are good.
FOL: all x. (EnvironmentFriendly(x) -> Good(x))
TEXT: A worksheet is either paper or environment-friendly.
FOL: ((Paper(Worksheet) & -EnvironmentFriendly(Worksheet)) | (-Paper(Worksheet) & EnvironmentFriendly(Worksheet)))
TEXT: A worksheet is not biodegradable.
FOL: -Dispensable(Worksheet)

ANSWER: Uncertain
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
A La Liga soccer team ranks higher than another La Liga soccer team if it receives more points.
If there are two La Liga soccer teams and neither has more points than the other, then the team which receives more points from the games between the two teams ranks higher.
Real Madrid and Barcelona are both La Liga soccer teams.
Real Madrid received more points than Barcelona.
Neither Real Madrid nor Barcelona received more points from the games between them.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
Real Madrid ranks higher than Barcelona.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>
TEXT: A La Liga soccer team ranks higher than another La Liga soccer team if it receives more points.
FOL: all x. all y. (LaLigaSoccerTeam(x) & LaLigaSoccerTeam(y) & MorePoints(x, y) -> RankHigherThan(x, y))
TEXT: If there are two La Liga soccer teams and neither has more points than the other, then the team which receives more points from the games between the two teams ranks higher.
FOL: all x. all y. (LaLigaSoccerTeam(x) & LaLigaSoccerTeam(y) & -MorePoints(x, y) & -MorePoints(y, x) & MorePointsInGameBetween(x, y) ->  RankHigherThan(x, y))
TEXT: Real Madrid and Barcelona are both La Liga soccer teams.
FOL: LaLigaSoccerTeam(RealMadrid) & LaLigaSoccerTeam(Barcelona)
TEXT: Real Madrid received more points than Barcelona.
FOL: MorePoints(RealMadrid, Barcelona)
TEXT: Neither Real Madrid nor Barcelona received more points from the games between them.
FOL: -MorePointsInGameBetween(RealMadrid, Barcelona) & -MorePointsInGameBetween(Barcelona, RealMadrid)
TEXT: Real Madrid ranks higher than Barcelona.
FOL: HigherRank(RealMadrid, Barcelona)

ANSWER: True
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
All professional athletes spend most of their time on sports.
All Olympic gold medal winners are professional athletes.
No full-time scientists spend the majority of their time on sports.
All Nobel physics laureates are full-time scientists.
Amy spends the most time on sports, or Amy is an Olympic gold medal winner.
If Amy is not a Nobel physics laureate, then Amy is not an Olympic gold medal winner.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
If Amy is not an Olympic gold medal winner, then Amy is a Nobel physics laureate.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>
TEXT: All professional athletes spend most of their time on sports.
FOL: all x. (ProfessionalAthlete(x) -> SpendOn(x, MostOfTheirTime, Sports))
TEXT: All Olympic gold medal winners are professional athletes.
FOL: all x. (OlympicGoldMedalWinner(x) -> ProfessionalAthlete(x))
TEXT: No full-time scientists spend the majority of their time on sports.
FOL: all x. (FullTimeScientist(x) -> -SpendOn(x, MostOfTheirTime, Sports))
TEXT: All Nobel physics laureates are full-time scientists.
FOL: all x. (NobelPhysicsLaureate(x) -> FullTimeScientist(x))
TEXT: Amy spends the most time on sports, or Amy is an Olympic gold medal winner.
FOL: SpendOn(Amy, MostOfTheirTime, Sports) | OlympicGoldMedalWinner(Amy)
TEXT: If Amy is not a Nobel physics laureate, then Amy is not an Olympic gold medal winner.
FOL: -NobelPhysicsLaureate(Amy) -> -OlympicGoldMedalWinner(Amy)
TEXT: If Amy is not an Olympic gold medal winner, then Amy is a Nobel physics laureate.
FOL: -OlympicGoldMedalWinner(Amy) -> NobelLaureate(Amy)

ANSWER: False
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>

Everything that requires talent requires practice.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>

</CONCLUSION>

=== Example 69 ===
Prompt:
The following is a first-order logic (FOL) problem.
The problem is to determine whether the conclusion follows from the premises.
The premises are given in the form of a set of first-order logic sentences.
The conclusion is given in the form of a single first-order logic sentence.
The task is to translate each of the premises and conclusions into FOL expressions.and then to evaluate the conclusion as ANSWER: True, ANSWER: False, or ANSWER: Uncertain given the premises. The output should follow format TEXT: 
FOL: 
TEXT: 
FOL:... ANSWER: 


<PREMISES>
All biodegradable things are environment-friendly.
All woodware is biodegradable.
All paper is woodware.
Nothing is a good thing and also a bad thing.
All environment-friendly things are good.
A worksheet is either paper or environment-friendly.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
A worksheet is not biodegradable.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>
TEXT: All biodegradable things are environment-friendly.
FOL: all x. (Biodegradable(x) -> EnvironmentFriendly(x))
TEXT: All woodware is biodegradable.
FOL: all x. (Woodware(x) -> Biodegradable(x))
TEXT: All paper is woodware.
FOL: all x. (Paper(x) -> Woodware(x))
TEXT: Nothing is a good thing and also a bad thing.
FOL: -(exists x. (Good(x) & Bad(x)))
TEXT: All environment-friendly things are good.
FOL: all x. (EnvironmentFriendly(x) -> Good(x))
TEXT: A worksheet is either paper or environment-friendly.
FOL: ((Paper(Worksheet) & -EnvironmentFriendly(Worksheet)) | (-Paper(Worksheet) & EnvironmentFriendly(Worksheet)))
TEXT: A worksheet is not biodegradable.
FOL: -Dispensable(Worksheet)

ANSWER: Uncertain
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
A La Liga soccer team ranks higher than another La Liga soccer team if it receives more points.
If there are two La Liga soccer teams and neither has more points than the other, then the team which receives more points from the games between the two teams ranks higher.
Real Madrid and Barcelona are both La Liga soccer teams.
Real Madrid received more points than Barcelona.
Neither Real Madrid nor Barcelona received more points from the games between them.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
Real Madrid ranks higher than Barcelona.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>
TEXT: A La Liga soccer team ranks higher than another La Liga soccer team if it receives more points.
FOL: all x. all y. (LaLigaSoccerTeam(x) & LaLigaSoccerTeam(y) & MorePoints(x, y) -> RankHigherThan(x, y))
TEXT: If there are two La Liga soccer teams and neither has more points than the other, then the team which receives more points from the games between the two teams ranks higher.
FOL: all x. all y. (LaLigaSoccerTeam(x) & LaLigaSoccerTeam(y) & -MorePoints(x, y) & -MorePoints(y, x) & MorePointsInGameBetween(x, y) ->  RankHigherThan(x, y))
TEXT: Real Madrid and Barcelona are both La Liga soccer teams.
FOL: LaLigaSoccerTeam(RealMadrid) & LaLigaSoccerTeam(Barcelona)
TEXT: Real Madrid received more points than Barcelona.
FOL: MorePoints(RealMadrid, Barcelona)
TEXT: Neither Real Madrid nor Barcelona received more points from the games between them.
FOL: -MorePointsInGameBetween(RealMadrid, Barcelona) & -MorePointsInGameBetween(Barcelona, RealMadrid)
TEXT: Real Madrid ranks higher than Barcelona.
FOL: HigherRank(RealMadrid, Barcelona)

ANSWER: True
</EVALUATE>

=== Example 71 ===
Prompt:
The following is a first-order logic (FOL) problem.
The problem is to determine whether the conclusion follows from the premises.
The premises are given in the form of a set of first-order logic sentences.
The conclusion is given in the form of a single first-order logic sentence.
The task is to translate each of the premises and conclusions into FOL expressions.and then to evaluate the conclusion as ANSWER: True, ANSWER: False, or ANSWER: Uncertain given the premises. The output should follow format TEXT: 
FOL: 
TEXT: 
FOL:... ANSWER: 


<PREMISES>
All biodegradable things are environment-friendly.
All woodware is biodegradable.
All paper is woodware.
Nothing is a good thing and also a bad thing.
All environment-friendly things are good.
A worksheet is either paper or environment-friendly.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
A worksheet is not biodegradable.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>
TEXT: All biodegradable things are environment-friendly.
FOL: all x. (Biodegradable(x) -> EnvironmentFriendly(x))
TEXT: All woodware is biodegradable.
FOL: all x. (Woodware(x) -> Biodegradable(x))
TEXT: All paper is woodware.
FOL: all x. (Paper(x) -> Woodware(x))
TEXT: Nothing is a good thing and also a bad thing.
FOL: -(exists x. (Good(x) & Bad(x)))
TEXT: All environment-friendly things are good.
FOL: all x. (EnvironmentFriendly(x) -> Good(x))
TEXT: A worksheet is either paper or environment-friendly.
FOL: ((Paper(Worksheet) & -EnvironmentFriendly(Worksheet)) | (-Paper(Worksheet) & EnvironmentFriendly(Worksheet)))
TEXT: A worksheet is not biodegradable.
FOL: -Dispensable(Worksheet)

ANSWER: Uncertain
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
A La Liga soccer team ranks higher than another La Liga soccer team if it receives more points.
If there are two La Liga soccer teams and neither has more points than the other, then the team which receives more points from the games between the two teams ranks higher.
Real Madrid and Barcelona are both La Liga soccer teams.
Real Madrid received more points than Barcelona.
Neither Real Madrid nor Barcelona received more points from the games between them.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
Real Madrid ranks higher than Barcelona.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>
TEXT: A La Liga soccer team ranks higher than another La Liga soccer team if it receives more points.
FOL: all x. all y. (LaLigaSoccerTeam(x) & LaLigaSoccerTeam(y) & MorePoints(x, y) -> RankHigherThan(x, y))
TEXT: If there are two La Liga soccer teams and neither has more points than the other, then the team which receives more points from the games between the two teams ranks higher.
FOL: all x. all y. (LaLigaSoccerTeam(x) & LaLigaSoccerTeam(y) & -MorePoints(x, y) & -MorePoints(y, x) & MorePointsInGameBetween(x, y) ->  RankHigherThan(x, y))
TEXT: Real Madrid and Barcelona are both La Liga soccer teams.
FOL: LaLigaSoccerTeam(RealMadrid) & LaLigaSoccerTeam(Barcelona)
TEXT: Real Madrid received more points than Barcelona.
FOL: MorePoints(RealMadrid, Barcelona)
TEXT: Neither Real Madrid nor Barcelona received more points from the games between them.
FOL: -MorePointsInGameBetween(RealMadrid, Barcelona) & -MorePointsInGameBetween(Barcelona, RealMadrid)
TEXT: Real Madrid ranks higher than Barcelona.
FOL: HigherRank(RealMadrid, Barcelona)

ANSWER: True
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
All professional athletes spend most of their time on sports.
All Olympic gold medal winners are professional athletes.
No full-time scientists spend the majority of their time on sports.
All Nobel physics laureates are full-time scientists.
Amy spends the most time on sports, or Amy is an Olympic gold medal winner.
If Amy is not a Nobel physics laureate, then Amy is not an Olympic gold medal winner.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
If Amy is not an Olympic gold medal winner, then Amy is a Nobel physics laureate.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>
TEXT: All professional athletes spend most of their time on sports.

FOL: all x. (OlympicGoldMedalWinner(x) -> ProfessionalAthlete(x))

TEXT: If Amy is not an Olympic gold medal winner, then Amy is a Nobel physics laureate.
FOL: -OlympicGoldMedalWinner(Amy) -> NobelLaureate(Amy)

ANSWER: False
</EVALUATE>

=== Example 74 ===
Prompt:
The following is a first-order logic (FOL) problem.
The problem is to determine whether the conclusion follows from the premises.
The premises are given in the form of a set of first-order logic sentences.
The conclusion is given in the form of a single first-order logic sentence.
The task is to translate each of the premises and conclusions into FOL expressions.and then to evaluate the conclusion as ANSWER: True, ANSWER: False, or ANSWER: Uncertain given the premises. The output should follow format TEXT: 
FOL: 
TEXT: 
FOL:... ANSWER: 


<PREMISES>
All biodegradable things are environment-friendly.
All woodware is biodegradable.
All paper is woodware.
Nothing is a good thing and also a bad thing.
All environment-friendly things are good.
A worksheet is either paper or environment-friendly.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
A worksheet is not biodegradable.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>
TEXT: All biodegradable things are environment-friendly.
FOL: all x. (Biodegradable(x) -> EnvironmentFriendly(x))
TEXT: All woodware is biodegradable.
FOL: all x. (Woodware(x) -> Biodegradable(x))
TEXT: All paper is woodware.
FOL: all x. (Paper(x) -> Woodware(x))
TEXT: Nothing is a good thing and also a bad thing.
FOL: -(exists x. (Good(x) & Bad(x)))
TEXT: All environment-friendly things are good.
FOL: all x. (EnvironmentFriendly(x) -> Good(x))
TEXT: A worksheet is either paper or environment-friendly.
FOL: ((Paper(Worksheet) & -EnvironmentFriendly(Worksheet)) | (-Paper(Worksheet) & EnvironmentFriendly(Worksheet)))
TEXT: A worksheet is not biodegradable.
FOL: -Dispensable(Worksheet)

ANSWER: Uncertain
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
A La Liga soccer team ranks higher than another La Liga soccer team if it receives more points.
If there are two La Liga soccer teams and neither has more points than the other, then the team which receives more points from the games between the two teams ranks higher.
Real Madrid and Barcelona are both La Liga soccer teams.
Real Madrid received more points than Barcelona.
Neither Real Madrid nor Barcelona received more points from the games between them.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
Real Madrid ranks higher than Barcelona.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>
TEXT: A La Liga soccer team ranks higher than another La Liga soccer team if it receives more points.
FOL: all x. all y. (LaLigaSoccerTeam(x) & LaLigaSoccerTeam(y) & MorePoints(x, y) -> RankHigherThan(x, y))
TEXT: If there are two La Liga soccer teams and neither has more points than the other, then the team which receives more points from the games between the two teams ranks higher.
FOL: all x. all y. (LaLigaSoccerTeam(x) & LaLigaSoccerTeam(y) & -MorePoints(x, y) & -MorePoints(y, x) & MorePointsInGameBetween(x, y) ->  RankHigherThan(x, y))
TEXT: Real Madrid and Barcelona are both La Liga soccer teams.
FOL: LaLigaSoccerTeam(RealMadrid) & LaLigaSoccerTeam(Barcelona)
TEXT: Real Madrid received more points than Barcelona.
FOL: MorePoints(RealMadrid, Barcelona)
TEXT: Neither Real Madrid nor Barcelona received more points from the games between them.
FOL: -MorePointsInGameBetween(RealMadrid, Barcelona) & -MorePointsInGameBetween(Barcelona, RealMadrid)
TEXT: Real Madrid ranks higher than Barcelona.
FOL: HigherRank(RealMadrid, Barcelona)

ANSWER: True
</EVALUATE>

=== Example 77 ===
Prompt:
The following is a first-order logic (FOL) problem.
The problem is to determine whether the conclusion follows from the premises.
The premises are given in the form of a set of first-order logic sentences.
The conclusion is given in the form of a single first-order logic sentence.
The task is to translate each of the premises and conclusions into FOL expressions.and then to evaluate the conclusion as ANSWER: True, ANSWER: False, or ANSWER: Uncertain given the premises. The output should follow format TEXT: 
FOL: 
TEXT: 
FOL:... ANSWER: 


<PREMISES>
All biodegradable things are environment-friendly.
All woodware is biodegradable.
All paper is woodware.
Nothing is a good thing and also a bad thing.
All environment-friendly things are good.
A worksheet is either paper or environment-friendly.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
A worksheet is not biodegradable.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>
TEXT: All biodegradable things are environment-friendly.
FOL: all x. (Biodegradable(x) -> EnvironmentFriendly(x))
TEXT: All woodware is biodegradable.
FOL: all x. (Woodware(x) -> Biodegradable(x))
TEXT: All paper is woodware.
FOL: all x. (Paper(x) -> Woodware(x))
TEXT: Nothing is a good thing and also a bad thing.
FOL: -(exists x. (Good(x) & Bad(x)))
TEXT: All environment-friendly things are good.
FOL: all x. (EnvironmentFriendly(x) -> Good(x))
TEXT: A worksheet is either paper or environment-friendly.
FOL: ((Paper(Worksheet) & -EnvironmentFriendly(Worksheet)) | (-Paper(Worksheet) & EnvironmentFriendly(Worksheet)))
TEXT: A worksheet is not biodegradable.
FOL: -Dispensable(Worksheet)

ANSWER: Uncertain
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
A La Liga soccer team ranks higher than another La Liga soccer team if it receives more points.
If there are two La Liga soccer teams and neither has more points than the other, then the team which receives more points from the games between the two teams ranks higher.
Real Madrid and Barcelona are both La Liga soccer teams.
Real Madrid received more points than Barcelona.
Neither Real Madrid nor Barcelona received more points from the games between them.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
Real Madrid ranks higher than Barcelona.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>
TEXT: A La Liga soccer team ranks higher than another La Liga soccer team if it receives more points.
FOL: all x. all y. (LaLigaSoccerTeam(x) & LaLigaSoccerTeam(y) & MorePoints(x, y) -> RankHigherThan(x, y))

TEXT: Real Madrid and Barcelona are both La Liga soccer teams.
FOL: LaLigaSoccerTeam(RealMadrid) & LaLigaSoccerTeam(Barcelona)
TEXT: Real Madrid received more points than Barcelona.
FOL: MorePoints(RealMadrid, Barcelona)
TEXT: Neither Real Madrid nor Barcelona received more points from the games between them.
FOL: -MorePointsInGameBetween(RealMadrid, Barcelona) & -MorePointsInGameBetween(Barcelona, RealMadrid)
TEXT: Real Madrid ranks higher than Barcelona.
FOL: HigherRank(RealMadrid, Barcelona)

ANSWER: True
</EVALUATE>

=== Example 79 ===
Prompt:
The following is a first-order logic (FOL) problem.
The problem is to determine whether the conclusion follows from the premises.
The premises are given in the form of a set of first-order logic sentences.
The conclusion is given in the form of a single first-order logic sentence.
The task is to translate each of the premises and conclusions into FOL expressions.and then to evaluate the conclusion as ANSWER: True, ANSWER: False, or ANSWER: Uncertain given the premises. The output should follow format TEXT: 
FOL: 
TEXT: 
FOL:... ANSWER: 


<PREMISES>
All biodegradable things are environment-friendly.
All woodware is biodegradable.
All paper is woodware.
Nothing is a good thing and also a bad thing.
All environment-friendly things are good.
A worksheet is either paper or environment-friendly.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
A worksheet is not biodegradable.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>
TEXT: All biodegradable things are environment-friendly.
FOL: all x. (Biodegradable(x) -> EnvironmentFriendly(x))
TEXT: All woodware is biodegradable.
FOL: all x. (Woodware(x) -> Biodegradable(x))
TEXT: All paper is woodware.
FOL: all x. (Paper(x) -> Woodware(x))
TEXT: Nothing is a good thing and also a bad thing.
FOL: -(exists x. (Good(x) & Bad(x)))
TEXT: All environment-friendly things are good.
FOL: all x. (EnvironmentFriendly(x) -> Good(x))
TEXT: A worksheet is either paper or environment-friendly.
FOL: ((Paper(Worksheet) & -EnvironmentFriendly(Worksheet)) | (-Paper(Worksheet) & EnvironmentFriendly(Worksheet)))
TEXT: A worksheet is not biodegradable.
FOL: -Dispensable(Worksheet)

ANSWER: Uncertain
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
A La Liga soccer team ranks higher than another La Liga soccer team if it receives more points.
If there are two La Liga soccer teams and neither has more points than the other, then the team which receives more points from the games between the two teams ranks higher.
Real Madrid and Barcelona are both La Liga soccer teams.
Real Madrid received more points than Barcelona.
Neither Real Madrid nor Barcelona received more points from the games between them.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
Real Madrid ranks higher than Barcelona.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>
TEXT: A La Liga soccer team ranks higher than another La Liga soccer team if it receives more points.
FOL: all x. all y. (LaLigaSoccerTeam(x) & LaLigaSoccerTeam(y) & MorePoints(x, y) -> RankHigherThan(x, y))
TEXT: If there are two La Liga soccer teams and neither has more points than the other, then the team which receives more points from the games between the two teams ranks higher.
FOL: all x. all y. (LaLigaSoccerTeam(x) & LaLigaSoccerTeam(y) & -MorePoints(x, y) & -MorePoints(y, x) & MorePointsInGameBetween(x, y) ->  RankHigherThan(x, y))
TEXT: Real Madrid and Barcelona are both La Liga soccer teams.
FOL: LaLigaSoccerTeam(RealMadrid) & LaLigaSoccerTeam(Barcelona)
TEXT: Real Madrid received more points than Barcelona.
FOL: MorePoints(RealMadrid, Barcelona)
TEXT: Neither Real Madrid nor Barcelona received more points from the games between them.
FOL: -MorePointsInGameBetween(RealMadrid, Barcelona) & -MorePointsInGameBetween(Barcelona, RealMadrid)
TEXT: Real Madrid ranks higher than Barcelona.
FOL: HigherRank(RealMadrid, Barcelona)

ANSWER: True
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
All professional athletes spend most of their time on sports.
All Olympic gold medal winners are professional athletes.
No full-time scientists spend the majority of their time on sports.
All Nobel physics laureates are full-time scientists.
Amy spends the most time on sports, or Amy is an Olympic gold medal winner.
If Amy is not a Nobel physics laureate, then Amy is not an Olympic gold medal winner.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
If Amy is not an Olympic gold medal winner, then Amy is a Nobel physics laureate.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>
TEXT: All professional athletes spend most of their time on sports.
FOL: all x. (ProfessionalAthlete(x) -> SpendOn(x, MostOfTheirTime, Sports))
TEXT: All Olympic gold medal winners are professional athletes.
FOL: all x. (OlympicGoldMedalWinner(x) -> ProfessionalAthlete(x))
TEXT: No full-time scientists spend the majority of their time on sports.
FOL: all x. (FullTimeScientist(x) -> -SpendOn(x, MostOfTheirTime, Sports))
TEXT: All Nobel physics laureates are full-time scientists.
FOL: all x. (NobelPhysicsLaureate(x) -> FullTimeScientist(x))
TEXT: Amy spends the most time on sports, or Amy is an Olympic gold medal winner.
FOL: SpendOn(Amy, MostOfTheirTime, Sports) | OlympicGoldMedalWinner(Amy)
TEXT: If Amy is not a Nobel physics laureate, then Amy is not an Olympic gold medal winner.
FOL: -NobelPhysicsLaureate(Amy) -> -OlympicGoldMedalWinner(Amy)
TEXT: If Amy is not an Olympic gold medal winner, then Amy is a Nobel physics laureate.
FOL: -OlympicGoldMedalWinner(Amy) -> NobelLaureate(Amy)

ANSWER: False
</EVALUATE>

</PREMISES>

</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>

Explanation:
Given the premises, we know that there exist birds that are hawks and that no hawk swims. Therefore, since some birds are hawks, and these hawks do not swim, it cannot be true that all birds swim. Hence, the conclusion "All birds swim" is false based on the provided premises.
